Ruling on al-Ta'rif (Gathering on Arafah Day)
Critical refinement: declares al-ta'rif as bid'ah and disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on al-ta'rif and explain why it is considered makruh and bid'ah.

Core Idea
Gathering on Arafah day in imitation of Hajj is a disliked innovation (makruh bid'ah) in the Hanafi school.

Al-ta'rif refers to the practice of gathering on the day of Arafah to stand and pray, imitating the pilgrims at Arafat. While some may see it as a meritorious act, the Hanafi school, based on careful reasoning, considers it a disliked innovation. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the reasoning behind it, and the internal scholarly discussion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that al-ta'rif is a gathering on Arafah day with standing and uncovering heads, mimicking the Hajj ritual. The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) and a bid'ah (innovation).
2
Understand the reasoning
The passage argues that standing (wuquf) is a specific act of worship tied to Hajj; replicating it elsewhere does not make it worship and risks creedal harm. Imitation alone, even without intent, is problematic.
The key principle: worship acts are tawqifi (divinely prescribed) and cannot be innovated.
3
Note the internal ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that the practice is permissible, but scholars interpret this as restricted to gatherings without standing and uncovering heads.
Al-Kamal and the author of al-Durar emphasize the restrictive interpretation.
4
Conclude with mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is makruh, and avoiding the practice cuts off potential creedal confusion among the common people.
This is the view preferred by later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتعريف ليس بشيء معتبر فهو غير مسنون وغير مستحب، وسئل الإمام مالك عن ذلك، فقال: وإنما مفاتح هذه الأشياء البدع، كذا في « الدراية »، وقاله الكمال: والأولى الكراهة؛ لأن الوقوف عهد قربة في مكان مخصوص فلا يكون قربة في غيره. وفي ( الدرر والغرر »: ( : الصحيح الكراهة، ولا . يجوز [ الاختراع ] ) في الدين (۳) ، كذا في «الكافي، وفي المنع منه حسم لمفسدة اعتقادية تُتُوقَّع من العوام، ونفس الوقوف، وكشف الرؤوس يستلزم التشبه وإن لم يقصد، ويحمل ما ذكره في « الكافي» بقوله: وعن أبي حنيفة أنه ليس بسنة، وإنما هو حدث أحدثه الناس فمن فعله جاز انتهى، على كونه بلا وقوف وكشف الرؤوس قاله الكمال.
And al-ta'rif is not a considered thing; it is not sunnah and not recommended. Imam Malik was asked about that and said: The keys of these matters are innovations. This is in al-Diraya. And al-Kamal said: The better view is dislike, because standing (wuquf) is an act of worship in a specific place, so it is not an act of worship elsewhere. And in al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: The correct view is dislike, and innovation in religion is not permissible. This is in al-Kafi. And prohibiting it cuts off a creedal harm that is feared from the common people. And the action of standing and uncovering heads entails imitation even if not intended. And what was mentioned in al-Kafi from Abu Hanifa that it is not sunnah but only an event people innovated, and if someone does it it is permissible, is interpreted as being without standing and uncovering heads, according to al-Kamal.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement regarding the practice known as al-ta'rif, which is a gathering on the day of Arafah by those not on pilgrimage. The author firmly states that this practice is not considered (laysa bi-shay) in the law; it is neither sunnah nor mustahabb. It quotes Imam Malik calling it bid'ah (innovation). The preferred view (al-awla) is that it is makruh (disliked). The reasoning is that standing at Arafah is a specific act of worship tied to the Hajj, so replicating it elsewhere is not a form of worship. The text warns of creedal harm to common people who may think it is sunnah. It also mentions that the mere act of standing and uncovering heads (though not intended to imitate) resembles the pilgrims in Arafah. The quote from Abu Hanifa that it is not sunnah but an innovation is interpreted to mean that if done without the specific standing and uncovering heads, it is permissible, but otherwise it is makruh.

Key Terms
التعريف (al-ta'rif): The practice of gathering on the day of Arafah and standing in a place, imitating the pilgrims at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the practice of al-ta'rif (gathering on the day of Arafah)?
A) Sunnah and recommended
B) Makruh (disliked) and considered bid'ah
C) Mubah (permissible) without restriction
D) Fard (obligatory) for those not on Hajj

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers al-ta'rif (gathering on Arafah day in imitation of Hajj) a makruh innovation, and the relied-upon position is to avoid it to prevent religious innovation.

Definition of Janazah and Positioning of the Dying Person
Definition and initial rulings for the dying person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of janazah and explain the sunnah and permissible positions for the dying person, including conditions for each.

Core Idea
Sunnah to turn the dying on his right side; back is permissible with raised head for qibla.

The chapter on funerals begins with the definition of 'janazah'—a term with specific technical usage—and the initial care for the dying person. This lesson covers the recommended positioning towards qibla and the Hanafi view that allows an easier alternative, ensuring dignity and proper orientation.

Guided Path
1
Define janazah linguistically and technically
Identify the linguistic variations (fatḥ vs kasr) and al-Azharī’s technical definition: the deceased wrapped on the bier. This sets the scope for the chapter.
Hanafis follow al-Azharī’s distinction.
2
Identify the ruling for turning the dying
State that it is sunnah (recommended) to turn the muḥtaḍar on his right side toward qibla, based on the transmitted sunnah and his future placement in the grave.
This is the primary Hanafi position.
3
Note the permissible alternative
Recognise that laying the dying person on his back is permissible, preferred by Transoxiana scholars for ease of treatment, with the condition that the head is raised so the face points to qibla.
Both positions are within the school; the sunnah is the right side.
4
List the signs of dying
The passage mentions relaxation of feet, sunken temples, bent nose, and dangling scrotal skin as indicators of imminent death, prompting the application of these rulings.
These signs are practical for caregivers.

Chapter on rulings of funerals. It is sunnah to turn the dying person on his right side, and it is permissible to lie on his back, and his head is raised slightly. And he is prompted with the mention of the shahada near him. Chapter on rulings of funerals. Janāzah (plural) — with fatḥ and kasr — derived from janaztu al-shay’ ajanuzuhu, from the pattern of ḍaraba, meaning I covered it. Al-Asma‘ī and Ibn al-A‘rābī said: with kasr, it is the deceased himself; with fatḥ, it is the bier. From Tha‘lab: the opposite. Al-Azharī said: it is not called janāzah until the deceased is bound on it wrapped in a shroud. (It is sunnah to turn the dying person) i.e., one who is near death, described as such due to the presence of his death or the angels of death. Signs of dying: relaxation of his feet, sinking of his temples, bending of his nose, and extension of the skin of his testicles, because the testicle hangs at death and its skin dangles. At that point, he is turned towards the qibla on his right side, because it is the transmitted sunnah, and because he will be placed in the grave on his right side, so he is given the ruling of what is near it. (And it is permissible to lie on his back) chosen by our mashāyikh of Transoxiana, because it is easier for treating him. (But) (his head is raised slightly so that his face is towards the qibla and not the sky). (And) it is sunnah to prompt him, that is, (with the mention of the testimony at his side) due to his statement: “Prompt your dying ones: Lā ilāha illallāh, for there is no Muslim who says it at the time of death except that it saves him from the Fire” (reported by Ibn Abi Shayba). And due to his statement, peace be upon him: “Whoever’s last words are Lā ilāha illallāh enters Paradise” (reported by Abu Dawud and Ahmad). Thus it is in al-Burhān, i.e., he enters Paradise with the winners; otherwise every Muslim, even a sinful one, enters Paradise, even if after long punishment. And he only confined it to the mention of the shahada following the authentic hadith, although it was said in al-Mustasfā and others like al-Durar: “Prompt with both testimonies: Lā ilāha illallāh Muḥammad Rasūl Allāh,” and his reasoning in al-Durar that the first is not accepted without the second is not absolute, because that applies to a non-believer, and our speech is about prompting a believer. For this reason, Shaykh al-Islām Ibn Ḥajar among the Shāfi‘ī imams said: “The statement of a group that he is prompted with ‘Muḥammad Rasūl Allāh’ is rejected, because he is already a Muslim; the goal is that his speech ends with Lā ilāha illallāh so that he obtains that reward. As for the disbeliever, he is definitely prompted with both along with the word ‘ashhadu’ due to its obligation, for he does not become Muslim except with both.” End. That is due to the story of the Jews. Al-Bukhārī narrated. (1) Al-ṣudgh: the side of the face from the eye to the ear. Al-Mu‘jam al-Wasīṭ. (2) i.e., to close his eyes, tighten his jaws, and prevent curvature of his limbs. (3) Reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah in his Muṣannaf (2/447) similarly. (4) Reported by Abu Dawud in Funerals, Chapter on Talqeen (3116), and Ahmad in his Musnad (5/233). (5) What is between the brackets is missing from manuscript (B).
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on funeral rulings (Bāb Aḥkām al-Janā’iz) in the commentary. It begins by noting the linguistic variation of the word 'janāzah'—with kasr, it means the deceased; with fatḥ, the bier; but al-Azharī specifies that it is only called janāzah when the deceased is wrapped and placed on the bier. The main rulings concern the dying person (muḥtaḍar): it is sunnah to turn him towards the qibla on his right side, as this is the transmitted sunnah and because he will be placed on his right side in the grave. It is also permissible to lay him on his back, which is the preferred ruling of the Transoxiana scholars as it is easier for treatment, but then his head should be raised slightly so his face faces the qibla and not the sky. Then, it is sunnah to prompt (talqīn) him with the testimony (shahāda): 'Lā ilāha illallāh'. The proof is the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones with Lā ilāha illallāh' and 'Whoever’s last words are Lā ilāha illallāh enters Paradise.' The commentary addresses a dispute: some scholars (like the author of al-Mustasfā and al-Durar) say to prompt with both shahadas. The Hanafi response (and the view of Shaykh al-Islām Ibn Ḥajar al-‘Asqalānī, a Shafi‘i) is that for a Muslim, it is sufficient to prompt only with 'Lā ilāha illallāh', because the Muslim already believes in the second testimony. The mention of both is needed for a disbeliever to embrace Islam. The footnotes define 'ṣudgh' (temple) and indicate that the signs of dying are for medical care.

Key Terms
الجنازة (al-janāzah): The deceased after being wrapped in a shroud and placed on the bier; the word is used with fatḥ for the bier and kasr for the body, per al-Azharī.
المحتضر (al-muḥtaḍar): One who is near death, so called because death or the angels of death are present (ḥuḍūr).
السنة المنقولة (al-sunnah al-manqūlah): The transmitted practice of the Prophet (ﷺ), as opposed to sunnah derived from analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the sunnah position for a dying person?
A) Lying on the stomach facing the qibla
B) Sitting up facing the qibla
C) Turned on the right side facing the qibla
D) Lying on the back with head toward the qibla

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it is sunnah to position the dying person on his right side toward qibla, with a permissible alternative of laying him on his back with the head raised.

intermediate

Prompting the Dying with the Shahada: Rulings and Dispute
Ruling on prompting the dying with shahada and the related scholarly dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on talqin (prompting), cite the primary hadith evidence, and analyse the dispute over whether to prompt with one or both shahadas.

Core Idea
Prompt only 'Lā ilāha illallāh' for a Muslim; both testimonies for a disbeliever.

After positioning the dying person, the next recommended act is talqīn—prompting them to recite the shahada. This lesson examines the hadith evidence, the Hanafi position that a Muslim need only be prompted with the first testimony, and the opposing view that both are required. The practical difference is crucial for caregivers at the deathbed.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling for talqīn
Identify that prompting the dying with the testimony is sunnah (recommended) for a Muslim, based on the hadith.
The text uses 'yusannu an yulaqqana' (it is sunnah to prompt).
2
Cite the primary hadith evidence
The hadith 'Laqqinū mawtākum: lā ilāha illallāh' is the proof. Note its chain (Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abu Dawud, Ahmad) and that it is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The imperative indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
3
Explain the Hanafi position on content
For a Muslim, prompt only with 'Lā ilāha illallāh', because the Muslim already believes in Muḥammad as Messenger. The goal is to end with the first testimony for the specific reward.
This is supported by the wording of the hadith and by Ibn Hajar al-‘Asqalānī’s reasoning.
4
Analyse the opposing view
Some scholars (e.g., authors of al-Mustasfā, al-Durar) argue for both shahadas, reasoning that the first is not accepted without the second. Understand their proof.
This view is common among Shāfi‘īs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Hanafis use only the first testimony for a Muslim; others use both. For a disbeliever, both are wajib to enter Islam.
The passage explicitly addresses this distinction.

Source Text

Key Terms
تلقين (talqīn): Prompting the dying person to recite the shahada, a recommended (sunnah) practice in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on prompting a Muslim who is dying?
A) Prompt with both shahadas: 'Lā ilāha illallāh Muḥammad Rasūl Allāh'
B) Prompt only with 'Lā ilāha illallāh'
C) No prompting is required
D) Prompt only with 'Muḥammad Rasūl Allāh'

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, talqīn for a Muslim is sunnah and consists only of 'Lā ilāha illallāh'; both testimonies are required only for a non-Muslim to embrace Islam.

Recommended Actions at Time of Death and Immediately After
Rules for dying and deceased care

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommended actions for a dying person and immediately after death, apply the metaphorical interpretation of 'موتاكم', and explain the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Hanafis recite Surah Yaseen while the person is still alive, interpreting 'your dead' as the dying.

In this passage, the author outlines the sunan and mustahabbat (recommended acts) that surround the moment of death. These are acts of reverence and comfort for the dying and deceased, not obligations. We will walk through the actions, their textual proofs, and a key scholarly dispute about the timing of Quran recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended actions
List all actions mentioned for the dying (muhtadar) and after death, noting their ruling (mustahabb).
Actions: visiting the dying, reciting Yaseen, possibly Ra'd; after death: tying jaw, closing eyes with supplication, placing iron on stomach.
2
Locate the dalil for each action
Identify which hadith supports which action. The recitation is based on 'اقرؤوا على موتاكم يس' and the closing of eyes on 'إذا حضرتم موتاكم فأغمضوا البصر'.
The tying of jaw and placing iron are from practice (athar), not explicit hadith in this passage.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative form in the hadith indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul, not obligation (wujub).
Because these acts pertain to etiquette and there is no evidence of mandatory nature.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf on 'موتاكم'
Understand the dispute: Hanafis interpret 'موتاكم' metaphorically as the dying (muhtadar), while others take it literally as the dead. Trace the Hanafi response.
The dispute affects the timing of recitation (before vs after death).
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position reciting during death throes is relied upon. Note that all actions are mustahabb, not wajib.
The text does not mention a tarjih authority, but the interpretation is clear from the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسْتَحَبُّ لأقرباء المُحْتَضَر، وجيرانِهِ الدُخولُ عليه، ويَتْلُونَ عندَهُ سورةَ يبن . واستُحْسِنَ بَعْضُ الْمُتَأخَرِيْنَ سُورةَ الرَّعد. واختلفوا في إخراج الحائض والنفساء من عنده. فإذا مات شُدَّ لِحْيَاهُ، وغمض عيناه، ويقول مُغَمِّضُهُ: بِاسْمِ اللَّهِ، وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ سيدنا رسول الله، اللَّهُمَّ يَسِّر عليه أَمرَهُ، وسهل عليه ما بعده، وأسعده بلقائك، واجعل ما خرج إليه خيراً مما خرجَ عَنْهُ. ويُوضع على بطنه حديدة، لئلا ينتفخ. ودليله حديث: «اقْرَؤُوا عَلَى مَوْتَاكُمْ يبن» (رواه أبو داود وابن حبان وصححه) وحديث: «إِذَا حَضَرْتُمْ مَوْتَاكُمْ فَأَغْمِضُوا الْبَصَرَ» (رواه ابن ماجه وأحمد).
It is recommended for the relatives of the dying person and his neighbors to enter upon him, and they recite Surah Yaseen in his presence. And some later scholars considered Surah Ra'd good. And they differed regarding removing the menstruating woman and the postpartum woman from him. When he dies, his jaw is tied, his eyes are closed, and the one closing his eyes says: 'In the name of Allah, and upon the religion of our master the Messenger of Allah. O Allah, make his affair easy, and make what comes after easy for him, and make him happy with meeting You, and make what he has gone to better than what he has left.' And a piece of iron is placed on his stomach so that it does not swell. And its evidence is the hadith: 'Recite upon your dead Yaseen' (narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Hibban and authenticated) and the hadith: 'When you attend your dead, close the eyes' (narrated by Ibn Majah and Ahmad).
Source pages p. 570

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, expanded by the commentary of Imdad al-Fattah, covers the recommended practices (mustahabbat) surrounding death. It begins with the recommendation for relatives, friends, and neighbors to visit the dying person. This serves to fulfill their rights, provide comfort, and remind them of beneficial matters like making a will. The recitation of Surah Yaseen is based on the hadith 'Recite upon your dead Yaseen,' which is understood to refer to those in the throes of death (muhtadar), not the deceased. The wisdom is that Yaseen mentions the conditions of the Hereafter and resurrection, renewing the dying person's awareness. Some later scholars also recommended Surah Ra'd because it is said to ease the soul's departure. There is a difference of opinion about removing women who are menstruating or in postpartum from the dying person; the text notes the ikhtilaf but does not settle it. After death, immediate actions are: (1) tying the jaw with a wide band to keep it closed and prevent insects or water from entering during washing; (2) closing the eyes, based on the hadith that the eyes follow the soul, and the supplication said by the person closing them; (3) placing a piece of iron (or a heavy object) on the stomach to prevent bloating, as reported from al-Sha'bi and the practice of Anas. These are all sunan and demonstrate the comprehensive care for the dying and deceased in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
موتاكم (mawtākum): In the hadith, interpreted by Hanafis as those in the throes of death (muhtadar), not the deceased.
يبن (Yāsīn): Surah Yaseen, a chapter of the Quran, recited for its benefits for the dying.
لحية (liḥyah): Jaw; the bone that holds the teeth. Here, it refers to the lower jaw that is tied shut after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should Surah Yaseen be recited according to the hadith 'اقْرَؤُوا عَلَى مَوْتَاكُمْ يبن'?
A) After the person has died
B) While the person is in the throes of death
C) Only on the first night after burial
D) At the graveside during burial

Key Takeaway
All actions in this lesson are mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, and the interpretation of 'موتاكم' as the dying person governs the timing of Surah Yaseen recitation.

Sunnah of Carrying the Bier by Four Men
Stating the ruling on number of carriers and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of carriers for a funeral bier and identify when exceptions apply for children.

Core Idea
Four carriers is sunnah for an adult bier; one carrier suffices for a child.

When a Muslim passes away, carrying the bier is an act of respect and communal duty. But how many carriers are required? Is there a difference between an adult and a child? In this passage, the author clarifies the sunnah practice and the evidence behind it, including an important exception for young children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'Carrying it by four men is sunnah.' What is the act? Carrying the funeral bier. The ruling is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
Sunnah here means a rewarded act; omission is not sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. Look for the phrase 'When one of you follows the funeral bier, let him take hold of the four corners...' This is the primary proof.
The hadith is of ahad transmission (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove four carriers? The instruction to take the four corners implies that four people are needed, one for each corner. The phrase 'min al-sunnah' indicates recommendation.
Rational benefits (takhfif, honor, preventing resemblance to luggage) support the ruling.
4
Identify the exceptions
The passage then discusses a weaned child or similar. It says 'there is no harm if one person carries it in his hands.' So children are an exception; the sunnah of four carriers applies mainly to adults.
The exception is based on ease and practicality.
5
Note the disliked methods
Carrying on the back or on an animal is makruh (disliked). This is based on the principle of honoring the deceased and avoiding resemblance to luggage.
This reinforces the sunnah nature of the four-carrier method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حمل الجنازة ودفنها
يُسَنُ الحَمْلِهَا أربعة رجالٍ، لقول ابن مسعود له: إذا اتَّبَعَ أحدُكم الجَنَازَةَ فَلْيَأخُذ بقوائم السرير الأربعة، ثُمَّ لِيَتَطَوَّعَ بعد، أو ليدر، فإنَّهُ مِنَ السُّنَّةِ)، ولأنَّ فِيهِ تَخْفِيفَاً عَلَى الحَامِلين، وصيانة عن السقوط والانقلاب، وزيادة الإكرام للميت، والإسراع به وتكثير الجماعة، وهو أبعد من تشبيهه بحمل الأمتعة، ولذا يكره على الظهر والدابة، والصغير الفطيم أو نحوه لا بأس أن يحمله واحد على يديه، ويتداوله الناس بالحمل بأيديهم، وكذا حمله على يديه وهو راكب كذا في «شرح المقدسي » ، عن « الإسبيبجابي » ، وقال في ( التاتارخانية : والصغار من بني آدم مكرمون كالكبار، وعن «أبي حنيفة رحمه الله في الفطيم والرضيع: لا بأس بأن يحمل في الطبق، وإن حملـه الـرجــل الواحد أحب إلي، كذا في «الأصل».
Chapter on Carrying the Bier and Burying It. Carrying it by four men is sunnah, due to the statement of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): 'When one of you follows the funeral bier, let him take hold of the four corners of the bier, then he may volunteer thereafter, or join in, for it is from the sunnah.' And because it lightens the burden on the carriers, protects against falling and overturning, increases honor for the deceased, speeds up the procession, increases the congregation, and is farthest from resembling the carrying of luggage. Therefore, it is disliked to carry it on the back or on an animal. As for a small weaned child or similar, there is no harm if one person carries it in his hands, and people may take turns carrying it in their hands. Likewise, carrying it in his hands while riding. Thus in 'Sharh al-Maqdisi' from 'al-Isbījābī'. And it is said in al-Tātārkhāniyya: 'Small human beings are honored like adults.' And from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) regarding the weaned and suckling: 'There is no harm in carrying it on a tray, though I prefer that one man carries it.' Thus in al-Asl.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended number of carriers for a funeral bier. The author states that it is sunnah (recommended) to have four men carry the bier. The proof is a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud reporting that the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed followers of a funeral to take hold of the four corners of the bier. Additional rational arguments are given: it lightens the load on each carrier, prevents the bier from falling, shows greater respect for the deceased, allows faster walking, and distinguishes it from ordinary luggage. Due to this honor, the author notes that carrying the bier on one's back or on an animal is disliked (makruh). For small children (weaned or younger), the ruling is relaxed: one person may carry them in his hands, and it is also permissible to carry them on a tray. The preference according to Abu Hanifa is that a single person carries the child, but carrying on a tray is also allowed. This shows that the sunnah of four carriers applies primarily to adult funerals, while infants and young children are given special consideration.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; not obligatory but rewarded.
قوائم السرير (qawā'im al-sarīr): The four legs or corners of the bier (the structure on which the deceased is carried).
فطيم (faṭīm): A child who has been weaned (no longer nursing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One man
B) Two men
C) Four men
D) Six men

Key Takeaway
Four carriers are sunnah for an adult bier, but for children one carrier suffices, demonstrating the school's balance of honor and practicality.

Forty Steps and Order of Carrying the Bier
Explaining the recommended forty steps and the sequence of carrying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended order and number of steps for carrying the bier and identify the hadith proofs that establish this sunnah.

Core Idea
Carrying the bier forty steps in a specific order is a recommended sunnah expiating major sins.

Carrying the bier is a noble act in funeral rites. Our passage outlines the sunnah method: forty steps per carrier, with a precise sequence on the shoulders. The proofs come from two hadiths that highlight the spiritual reward and completeness of this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is describing (carrying the bier) and the legal status (mustahabb/recommended). Note that the forty steps and order are not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the two hadiths cited. The first mentions expiation of forty major sins; the second states that carrying on all four sides fulfills the duty.
Both hadiths are ahad (single-narrator) with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each proof supports the recommended practice. The explicit number 'forty' indicates the count; the mention of 'four sides' implies the order.
4
Describe the recommended order
Follow the sequence: right front on right shoulder, right rear on right shoulder, left front on left shoulder, left rear on left shoulder. Each side is carried for ten steps, totaling forty.
The bier's right side corresponds to the carrier's left because the deceased lies on his back.
5
Note the recommendation to hasten
The passage also recommends walking briskly with the bier, based on the hadith 'Hasten with the bier.'
This is separate from the forty steps but part of the overall sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي) لكل واحد (حَمْلُها أربعينَ خُطْوَةً. يبدأُ) الحامل بمُقَدَّمِها الأيمن فيضعه على يمينِهِ)، أي: على عاتقه الأيمن، ويَمِيْنُهَا) أي: الجنازة (مَا كَانَ جهَةَ يَسَارِ الحَامِلِ)، لأن الميت يلقى على ظهره، (ثُمَّ ) يضع (مُؤَخَّرِهَا الْأَيْمَنِ عَلَيْهِ) أَي: على عاتقه الأيمن، (ثُمَّ) يضع (مُقَدَّمَها الأيسر على يساره) أي: على عاتقه الأيسر، (ثم يَخْتِـم بـ:) الجانب ( الأيسر ) بحملها ( عليه ) أي: على عاتقه الأيسر، فيكون من كل جانب عشر خطوات، لقوله : ( مَنْ حَمَلَ جَنَازَةٌ أَرْبَعِينَ خَطْوَةً كَفَرَتْ عَنْهُ أرْبَعِينَ كَبِيرَةٌ » (٢) كذا في « التبيين، ولـقـول أبي هريرة: مَنْ حَمَلَ الجَنَازَةَ بِجَوَانِبِهَا الأَرَبَعِ فَقَدْ قَضَى الذِي عَلَيْهِ ، كذا في «الفتح». ويُسْتَحَبُّ الإسراع بها ) لقوله : ( أسْرِعُوا بِالجَنَازَةِ، فَإِنْ تَكُ صَالِحَةٌ فَخَيْرُ تُقَدِّمُونَهَا إِلَيهِ، وَإِنْ تَكُ غَيْرَ ذَلِكَ فَشَرٌّ
And it is befitting for each one to carry it forty steps. The carrier begins with its right front, placing it on his right (i.e. on his right shoulder). And its right (i.e. the bier's right) is whatever is on the left side of the carrier, because the deceased is placed on his back. Then he places its right rear on his right shoulder. Then he places its left front on his left shoulder. Then he concludes with the left side by carrying it on his left shoulder. Thus, from each side there are ten steps, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever carries a bier forty steps, forty major sins are expiated for him.' Thus in al-Tabyīn. And due to the saying of Abu Huraira: 'Whoever carries the bier on its four sides has fulfilled what is upon him.' Thus in al-Fatḥ. And it is recommended to hasten with it, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Hasten with the bier; if it is righteous, you are advancing it to good, and if it is otherwise, it is evil that you are putting off from your necks.'
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah method for carrying the bier. For each carrier, it is recommended to take forty steps with the bier on his shoulder. The order is specific: start with the right front corner on the right shoulder, then the right rear corner on the same shoulder, then the left front on the left shoulder, and finally the left rear on the left shoulder. This sequence ensures that each of the four sides is carried for ten steps, totaling forty steps. The proof comes from a hadith that carrying the bier forty steps expiates forty major sins, and another hadith that carrying it on all four sides fulfills the obligation. Additionally, it is recommended to walk briskly with the bier, based on the command to hasten with the funeral. This combination of steps and order is considered a complete sunnah practice.

Key Terms
خطوة (khuṭwah): A step; here specifically one pace while carrying the bier.
مقدمها الأيمن (muqaddamuhā al-ayman): The right front corner of the bier (from perspective of the carrier).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Walking Behind the Bier is Superior
Determining the preferred position for mourners relative to the bier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred position for mourners relative to the bier according to the Hanafi school, explain the evidence from hadith and Companion practice, and identify the conditions under which riding is permissible.

Core Idea
Walking behind the bier is more virtuous, but walking in front is permissible—especially to avoid crowding.

This lesson explores the proper etiquette for following a funeral bier. The Hanafi school, citing a powerful hadith, establishes that walking behind the bier is superior, likened to obligatory prayer over voluntary. However, the actions of the greatest Companions show that walking in front is not sinful, but rather a concession for ease. We will examine the evidence, the intra-school differences, and the conditions for riding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred position
Read the opening statement: 'Walking behind it is better than walking in front of it.' This is the core ruling. Note the explicit comparison to obligatory versus voluntary prayer, indicating the degree of preference.
The ruling is that walking behind is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage includes a hadith reported by a companion who heard it from the Prophet (peace be upon him) seven times. When questioned by Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about the basis, the narrator swore it was from the Prophet. This strengthens the proof.
The hadith directly states the virtue of walking behind.
3
Reconcile with Companion practice
Abu Sa'id observes that Abu Bakr and 'Umar sometimes walked in front. The narrator explains that they knew the virtue but chose to walk ahead to prevent crowding and make it easier for people. This shows permissibility for a valid reason.
The best of the ummah did it; thus it is not forbidden.
4
Analyze intra-Hanafi differences
The text presents differing views: Abu Hanifa allowed walking on any side without dislike, while Abu Yusuf disliked going ahead alone but allowed it if with a group. Note that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that walking behind is superior, but all positions are permissible.
The difference is about the degree of dislike, not prohibition.
5
Apply the ruling on riding
Riding in the funeral procession is permissible if one is far from the bier, but disliked if close. Additionally, riding ahead of the bier is disliked. This shows consideration for respect and avoiding disruption.
The key distinction is proximity to the bier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمشي خلفها أفضلُ مِنْ أمامها، كفَضْلِ صلاةِ الفَرْضِ على النفل، لقول عليه والذي بعث محمداً بالحق، إن فضل الماشي خلفها على الماشي أمامها، كفضل المكتوبة على التطوع، فقال أبو سعيد الخدري: أبرأيك تَقُولُ أَمْ بِشَيْءٍ سَمِعْتَهُ مِنْ رَسُولِ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فَغَضِبَ وَقَالَ: لا والله، بَلْ سَمِعْتُهُ غَيْرَ مَرَّةً ولا ثنتين ولا ثَلَاثَ، حَتَّى عَدَّ سَبْعَاً، فَقَالَ أَبُو سَعِيد: إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ أَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ يَمْشِيَانِ أَمَامَهَا، فَقَالَ عَلِيه : يَغْفِرُ الله لَهُمَا، لَقَدْ سَمِعَا ذَلِكَ مِنْ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كَمَا سَمِعْتُهُ، وإنَّهُما والله لَخَيْرُ هَذِهِ الأُمَّةِ، وَلَكِنَّهُمَا كَرهَا أنْ يَجْتَمِعَ النَّاسُ وَيَتَضَايَقُوا، فَاحَبًّا أَنْ يُسَهْلا عَلَى النَّاسِ)، ولقول أبي أمامة : إِنَّ رَسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مَشَى خَلْفَ جَنَازَةِ ابْنِهِ إِبْرَاهِيم حَافِياً، كذا في ( البرهان) والشفاعة في الصلاة، وهم يتأخرون عندها، ولأن الشفيع [ إنما يتقدم]) عادة إذا خيف عليه بطش المشفوع عنده فيمنعه الشفيع، ولا يتحقق ذلك هنا، كذا في « التبيين»، ويكره أن يتقدم الكل عليها، وإن كان كلهم خلفها فلا بأس، قال الحاكم» في « المنتقــى : وجدتُ في بعض الروايات أن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله قال: لا بأس بالمشي أمام الجنازة وخلفها، ويمنةً ويسرة، وكره « أبو يوسف رحمه الله أن يتقدمها منقطعاً عن القوم، فإذا كان مع جماعة فلا بأس بالمشي أمامها وخلفها ويمنة ويسرة، ولا بأس بالركوب في الجنازة قيل: هذا إذا بعد منها، أما إذا قرب منها فيكره، كذا في ( التاتارخانية»، وفي شرح المقدسي: ولا بأس بالركوب فيها، ويكره أن يتقدمها الراكب كذا في شرح المجمع لابن الضياء، وفي السنن عــن
And walking behind it is better than walking in front of it, like the superiority of obligatory prayer over voluntary prayer, due to his (peace be upon him) saying—and by Him who sent Muhammad with truth, indeed the virtue of the one walking behind it over the one walking in front of it is like the virtue of the obligatory over the supererogatory. Then Abu Sa'id al-Khudri said: 'Do you say this by your own opinion or from something you heard from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him)?' He became angry and said: 'No, by Allah, I heard it not once nor twice nor thrice, until he counted seven times.' So Abu Sa'id said: 'I saw Abu Bakr and 'Umar walking in front of it.' He (the narrator) said: 'May Allah forgive them both. They indeed heard that from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as I heard it, and by Allah they are the best of this ummah, but they disliked that the people crowd and become constrained, so they wanted to make it easy for the people.' And due to the saying of Abu Umamah: 'Indeed the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) walked behind the bier of his son Ibrahim barefoot.' Thus in al-Burhan. And the intercession in prayer, and they delay at it [unclear]. And because the intercessor only goes forward normally if he fears violence from the intercessee, but that is not the case here. Thus in al-Tabyīn. And it is disliked that all go ahead of it, but if all are behind it, there is no harm. Al-Hakim said in al-Muntaqā: 'I found in some narrations that Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: There is no harm in walking in front of the bier, behind it, to its right or left.' And Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) disliked that one go ahead of it separated from the people. If he is with the group, there is no harm in walking in front, behind, right, or left. And there is no harm in riding in the funeral procession. It was said: 'This is if he is far from it; if he is close, it is disliked.' Thus in al-Tātārkhāniyya. And in Sharh al-Maqdisi: 'There is no harm in riding in it, and it is disliked that the rider go ahead of it.' Thus in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Diya'. And in the Sunan from...
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage addresses the preferred position for those following the funeral bier. The clear ruling is that walking behind the bier is superior to walking in front, analogous to the superiority of obligatory prayer over voluntary prayer. This is supported by a hadith narrated with emphasis, where the companion swore he heard it multiple times. However, the actions of Abu Bakr and 'Umar, who sometimes walked in front, are explained: they did so to avoid crowding and to make it easier for people, not because they considered front walking better. Thus, the sunnah is to walk behind, but walking in front is permissible, especially if it serves a purpose like crowd management. The text then presents differing views within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa permitted walking on any side, while Abu Yusuf disliked walking in front alone but allowed it with the group. Regarding riding, it is permissible if one is far from the bier but disliked if close. The passage emphasizes that the virtue of walking behind is well-established, but practical concessions are made to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
المشي خلفها (al-mashy khalfahā): Walking behind the bier (in the funeral procession).
الركوب (al-rukūb): Riding (on an animal or vehicle) in the funeral procession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu Bakr and 'Umar do regarding the bier, and what was the reason?
A) They always walked behind; they followed the sunnah strictly.
B) They sometimes walked in front to avoid crowding.
C) They forbade walking behind; it was their personal opinion.
D) They walked in front because they considered it better.

Key Takeaway
Walking behind the bier is more virtuous, but walking in front is permitted, especially to ease crowding, as demonstrated by Abu Bakr and 'Umar.

Burial Sunnahs: Grave Type, Entry, and Supplication
Explaining burial sunnahs: grave type, entry direction, and supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on grave digging methods (lahd vs shaq), the proper way to enter the deceased into the grave, and the recommended supplication, and apply them to burial scenarios.

Core Idea
Lahd (niche) is the sunnah for Muslims; shaq (trench) is only for necessity in soft ground.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah (a commentary on Nur al-Idah) details the sunnan (recommended practices) of burial in the Hanafi school. It distinguishes between two methods of digging the grave, specifies how the deceased should be placed inside, and gives the exact wording of the supplication said at that moment. Understanding these details ensures that the final act of honouring the deceased is performed according to the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the two digging methods
Identify al-lahd (niche) and al-shaq (trench). Note that lahd is the preferred, sunnah method; shaq is only a substitute when the ground is soft.
Lahd = horizontal tunnel on the qibla side; shaq = vertical trench in the center.
2
Analyse the proof (dalil)
Examine the hadith 'al-lahdu lana wa al-shaqqu li-ghairina' and understand how the exclusive pronoun 'lana' establishes lahd as the prescribed method for Muslims.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and others; its transmission is sound (qati‘), but its indication (dalalah) is open to interpretation, hence the difference with Shafi‘is.
3
Determine the correct entry method
Learn that the deceased should be entered into the grave from the qibla side, not pulled in from the head or feet (sall). This honours the qibla and follows the practice of the Companions.
The term 'sall' (pulling) is discouraged; the preferred method is entering from above the qibla side.
4
Memorise the burial supplication
The person placing the body says: 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati rasulillah'. Understand the meaning: 'In the name of Allah we place you, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah we entrust you.'
This supplication is authentically reported from the Prophet ﷺ (Ibn Umar narration, sahih).

(و) يكره (الجُلوس قبل وضعها) عــن أعـنـاق الـرجــال، لقولـه عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( مَنْ تَبِعَ الجَنَازَةَ فَلا يَجْلِسُ حَتَّى تُوضَعَ ) وفي الجلوس قبل وضعه ازدراء به، كما في البرهان » ، و التبيين » ، ويُحْفَرُ القبرُ نصف قامة، أو إلى الصَّدْرِ، وَإِنْ زِيدَ كان حَسَناً) لأنه أبلغ في منع الرائحة والسباع، وفي ( الحجة ) : روى الحسن بن زياد » عن «أبي حنيفة » رحمه الله قال: طول القبر على قدر طول الإنسان، وعرضه قدر نصف ، قامة كذا في « التاتارخانية»، ويُلْحَدُ () إذا كانت الأرض صلبة، وهو أن يحفر في جانب القبلة من الـ حفيرة ولا يُشَقُّ إلا في أرض رخوَةٍ وَيُدْخَلُ المَيِّتُ مِنْ جِهَةِ القِبْلَةِ. ويقولُ واضعُهُ: بِاسْمِ اللهِ، وعلى مِلَّةِ سيدنا رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فيوضع الميت فيها، ولا يُشَقُّ)، وهو: أن يُحفر حفيرة في وسط القبر فيوضع فيها الميت، (إلا في أرض رخوَةٍ فلا بأس به فيها، ولا باتخاذ التابوت ولو من حديد، لكن السنة أن يفرش فيـه التراب، لقول رسول الله : « اللَّحْدُ لَنَا ، والشَّقُ لِغَيْرنَا » (۱) وقال ( الكمال » : واستحب بعض الصحابة أن في التراب رمساً (۳)، روي ذلك عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص، وقال: «لَيْسَ أَحَدُ جَنْبَيَّ أولَى بِالتُّرَابِ مِنَ الآخَرِ » ) انتهى. (وَيُدْخَلُ المَيِّتُ) في القبر (مِنْ جِهَةِ القبلة) إن أمكن، وهو أن توضع الجنازة إلى جانب القبلة من القبر، ويحمل الميت فيوضع في الأحد، فيكون الآخــذ لـه مستقبل القبلة حال الأخذ، كما فعله علي بابن المكفف ) ، وابن الحنفية بابن عباس ، ولأنه أدخل من قبل القبلة، ولم يسل سلا، ورفع قبره حتى يعرف، ولأن جهة القبلة أشرف، فكان أولى من السل، والسل يكون بالرأس وبالرجلين، فيدخل بأحدها ابتداء، ويقول واضعه) في قبره ما رواه ابن عمر : ( كانَ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أَدْخَلَ المَيِّتَ القَبْرَ قال: (بِاسْم الله، وعلى ملة رسول الله ) وقال : « إِذَا وَضَعْتُمْ مَوْتَاكُمْ فِي الْقَبْرِ فَقُولُوا: بِسْمِ اللَّهِ وَعَلَى مِلَّةِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ » صحيح على شرط الشيخين، قال شمس الأئمة ( السرخسي ) : أي : بسم الله وضعناك، وعلى ملة رسول الله (صلى الله عليه وسلم) سلمناك، وفي ( الظهيرية : إذا وضعوه قالوا: بسم الله وبالله وفي الله وعلى ملة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولا يضر دخول وتر أو شفع في القبر، لأن المقصود وضع الميت في القبر بقدر ما يحصل به الكفاية، وفي السغناقي» والسنة هو الوتر، وفي ( الحجة » : ويستحب أن يكونوا أقوياء أمناء صلحاء، وقـد صـح دخول قبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أربعة : علي والعباس وابنه الفضل، واختلف في الرابع: قيل: صهيب، أو
It is disliked to raise the voice with dhikr and to sit before it (the bier) is placed. The grave is dug half a man's height or up to the chest, and if increased, it is good. And one makes a lahd (niche) ... (2) Al-Mughirah reported that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The rider goes behind the funeral, and the walker walks ahead of it, close to it, on its right or left.' As in al-Burhan. Raising the voice with dhikr is disliked. In Sharh al-Tahawi: the follower of the funeral should be silent, and it is disliked for them to raise voice with dhikr or reciting Quran. In al-Zahiriyyah: if he wants to remember Allah, then in himself. From Ibrahim that it is disliked for a man walking with it to say: 'Ask forgiveness for him, may Allah forgive you.' In al-Sirajiyyah: their saying 'every living being will die' and the like behind the funeral is an innovation. In al-Khulasah: it is disliked for women to follow funerals; if there is a wailing woman with the funeral, she is rebuked and forbidden; if she does not desist, there is no harm in walking with her, and one disapproves inwardly. There is no harm in weeping in the house of the deceased; wailing, screaming, and tearing garments are disliked. One does not stand for a funeral that passes by if he does not intend to attend it, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. What has come of the command to stand for it is abrogated (3) by the command to sit, whether one is sitting on the road or at the grave, as in al-Tabyin. And it is disliked (to sit before it is placed) from the shoulders of the men, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever follows a funeral should not sit until it is placed.' Sitting before its placement is a form of disrespect, as in al-Burhan and al-Tabyin. The grave is dug half a man's height or up to the chest, and if increased, it is good, because it is more effective in preventing odor and beasts. In al-Hujjah: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) that he said: the length of the grave is according to the height of a man, and its width is half a man's height, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And one makes a lahd (niche) when the ground is solid, and it is to dig on the qibla side of the pit. And one does not make a shaq (trench) except in soft ground. And the deceased is entered from the direction of the qibla. The one placing him says: 'In the name of Allah, and upon the religion of our master, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' Then the deceased is placed in it. And one does not make a shaq (which is to dig a pit in the middle of the grave and place the deceased in it) except in soft ground; there is no harm in it then. And no use of a coffin, even if of iron, but the sunnah is to spread earth in it, because of the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'The lahd (niche) is for us, and the shaq (trench) is for others.' Al-Kamal said: Some companions recommended that in earth, rasm (covering with dust) - this is reported from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, who said: 'One side of me is not more entitled to the earth than the other.' End. And the deceased is entered into the grave from the direction of the qibla if possible, which is that the bier is placed on the qibla side of the grave, and the deceased is carried and placed in the lahd, so that the one taking him faces the qibla at the moment of taking, as Ali did with Ibn al-Mukaffif, and Ibn al-Hanafiyyah with Ibn Abbas; and because he was entered from the direction of the qibla, and not pulled, and his grave was raised so that it would be known; and because the qibla direction is more honorable, so it is preferable to pulling, and pulling is by the head or the feet, entering by one of them initially. And the one placing him says in his grave what Ibn Umar narrated: 'When the Prophet (peace be upon him) entered the deceased into the grave, he said: 'In the name of Allah, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah.' And he said: 'When you place your dead in the grave, say: In the name of Allah, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah.' It is sahih upon the condition of the two shaykhs. Shams al-Aimmah al-Sarakhsi said: i.e., 'In the name of Allah we place you, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah we entrust you.' In al-Zahiriyyah: when they place him, they say: 'In the name of Allah, and with Allah, and for Allah, and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' And it does not harm if an odd or even number enters the grave, because the objective is to place the deceased in the grave sufficiently. In al-Sughnaqi: and the sunnah is odd numbers. In al-Hujjah: it is recommended that they be strong, trustworthy, and righteous. It is established that four entered the grave of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): Ali, al-Abbas, his son al-Fadl, and there is disagreement about the fourth: it is said: Suhayb, or...
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the rulings related to the burial of the deceased. It covers several key points: First, it is makruh (disliked) to raise one's voice in dhikr or Quran while following the funeral; silence is recommended. Second, it is makruh to sit down before the bier is placed on the ground, as the hadith prohibits sitting until it is placed. Third, the depth of the grave is specified: half a man's height (approx. 3 cubits) or up to the chest, and deepening it is praiseworthy to prevent odors and beasts. Fourth, the preferred type of grave is al-lahd (a niche dug on the qibla side) for solid ground; al-shaq (a central trench) is only used in soft soil. This is based on the hadith 'al-lahd is for us, and al-shaq is for others.' Fifth, the deceased should be entered into the grave from the qibla side, not by pulling from the head or feet. Sixth, the one placing the deceased should say the supplication 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati rasulillah'. The commentary also notes that it is sunnah to have an odd number of people entering the grave, and they should be reliable and pious individuals. The passage also references the abrogation of standing for a funeral, citing that the command to stand was superseded by the command to sit.

Key Terms
اللحد (al-lahd): A niche dug on the qibla side of the grave where the deceased is placed.
الشق (al-shaq): A trench dug in the middle of the grave where the deceased is placed.
السل (al-sall): Pulling the deceased into the grave by the head or feet, as opposed to entering from the qibla side.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended type of grave when the ground is solid?
A) Shaq (trench)
B) Lahd (niche)
C) Both are equal
D) Use a coffin

Key Takeaway
Burial in the Hanafi school follows the sunnah of lahd (niche) in solid ground, entering from the qibla side, and reciting 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati rasulillah'.

Grave Shape and Prohibited Constructions
Ruling on grave shape and prohibited constructions with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on grave shape and identify which construction practices are prohibited or disliked.

Core Idea
The grave should be hump-shaped; squaring, plastering, and building for adornment are forbidden.

This lesson covers the sunnah of making the grave hump-shaped (tasnīm), the prohibition of making it square (tarbīʿ) and plastering (tajṣīṣ), and the prohibition of building structures for adornment. These rulings are derived from the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and explicit hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended shape
Find the ruling on the shape of the grave: it should be hump-shaped (musannam) like a camel's hump.
The height should be about a handspan or slightly more.
2
Locate the proof for tasnīm
The proof is the hadith of Sufyan al-Tammar who saw the Prophet's grave and those of Abu Bakr and Umar as hump-shaped.
3
Identify prohibited constructions
The text prohibits making the grave square (tarbīʿ) and plastering (tajṣīṣ) based on a hadith narrated by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan.
Building for adornment is haram; building for consolidation after burial is makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و أن يُ قبرها، لا قبره. ويُهال التراب، ويُسَنَّمُ القَبرُ ولا يُرَبَّعُ ويَحْرُمُ البناء عليه للزِّينةِ . ويكرهون الآجر، وبعض مشايخنا قالوا: إنما يكره الآجر إذا أُريد به الزينة، أما إذا أُريـد بـه دفـع أذى السباع، أو شيء آخر لا يكره، وفي ( الخانية»: يكره إذا كان مما يلي الميت، أما فيما وراء ذلك فلا بأس به، وفي « الحسامي » وقد رخص إسماعيل الزاهد بالآجر خلف اللبن عـلـى الـلحــد وأوصى به. وفي « المحيط » : قال مشایخ بخارى: لا يكره الآجر في بلدتنا المساس الحاجة إليه لضعف الأراضي، وما قيل: إن كراهة الآجر لمساس النار ليس بصحيح، لأن الكفن مسته النار ويغسل الميت بالماء الحار. (و) يستحب ( أنْ يُسَجَّى) أي يستر (قبرها) :أي: المرأة، لأن مبنى حالهن على الستر إلى أن يسوى عليها الأحد، و (لا) يسجى (قبره)، لأن عليه مر بقوم قد دفنوا ميتاً وبسطوا على قبره ثوباً فجذبه وقال: إنما يصنع هذا بالنساء)، إلا إذا كان لضرورة دفع مطر أو ثلج أو حــر عن الداخلين في القبر، فلا بأس به، ويُهالُ التُّرابُ في القبر للتوارث ستراً له، وإليه وقعت الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لِيُرِيَهُ كَيْفَ يُوَارِى سَوْءَةَ أَخِيهِ [للان : ٣١] ويستحب أن يحثي عليه التراب، لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى على جنازة، ثم أتى القبر فحتى عليه التراب من قبل رأسه ثلاثاً). ( ويُسَنَّمُ ) القبرُ ) ويكره أن يزيد فيه على التراب الذي خرج منه، ويجعله مرتفعاً عن الأرض مقـــدار شبر، أو أكثر بقليل لما روى البخاري عن سفيان التمار قال: دخلت البيـت الـذي فـيـه قـبـر الـنـبـي ‏، فرأيت قبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقبر أبي بكر وعمر مسنمة، ولا بأس برش، الماء عليه حفظاً لترابــه عـــن الاندراسه)، وعن أبي يوسف أنه كرهه، لأنه يجري مجرى التطيين، كذا في « البرهان». وفي التاتارخانية » : وإن خيف ذهاب أثره، فلا بأس برش الماء عليه بلا خلاف، إنمـا هـو فيما إذا لم يخف ذهاب أثره، ذكره في ظاهر الرواية» أنه لا يكره، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يكره، ولا يُرَبَّعُ) ولا يجصص، لما رواه ( محمد بن الحسن» في الآثار أخبرنا ( أبو حنيفة»، قال: حدثنـا شـيـخ لـنـا يرفعه إلى النبي أنه نهى عن تربيع القبُورِ وتَجْصِيصِهَا ) ويَحْرُمُ البناء عليه للزينة)، ويُكره للإحكام بعد الدفن، ولا بأس بالكتابة عليه، لئلا يذهب الأثر، ولا يُعْتَهَن. ويُكْرَهُ الدَّفن في البيوت، لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلامُ ويُكرهُ الدَّفْنُ فِي الفَسَاقِي ، . لما روينا (ويُكْرَهُ) البناء عليه (للإحكام بعدَ الدَّفنِ) لأن البناء للبقاء والقبر موضع الفناء، وأمـا قبل الدفن فليس بقبر. وفي « الفتاوى الكبرى » : والـيـوم اعتادوا التسنيم باللبن صيانة للقـبـر عـن النبش، ورأوا ذلك حسناً، وقال : « مَا رَآهُ المُسْلِمُونَ حَسَنَاً فَهُوَ عِنْدَ الله حَسَنٌ » وإن خيـف مـع التسنيم ورش الماء عليه فلا بأس بحجر يوضع أو أجر، فالآجر لا يـكــره عـلـى الظاهر، وفي «النوازل» : لا بأس بتطيينه، وفي ( الغياثية ) : وعليه الفتوى، كذا في ( التاتارخانية» وقد اعتاد أهـل مصر وضع الأحجار حفظاً للقبر عن الاندراس والنبش ولا بأس به، ولا (بالكتابة عليه، لئلا يذهب الأثر ) فيحترم للعلم بصاحبه ( ولا يُمْتَهَن)، وعن أبي يوسف أنـه يـكـره أن يكتـب عـلـيـه كتاباً. وفي ( الظهيرية » : ولو وضع عليه شيئاً من الأحجار، وكتب عليه شيئاً فلا بأس به عند البعض، لأنه « لما دفن عثمان بن مظعون أمر النبي رجلاً أن يأتيه بحجر فلم يستطع حمله، فقام إليـهـا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فَحَسَر عن ذِرَاعَيْهِ ثُمَّ حَمَلَهَا فَوَضَعَهَا عِنْدَ رَأْسِهِ، وَقَالَ: أَتَعْلَمُ بِهَا قَبْرَ أَخِي وَأَدْفِنُ إِلَيْهِ مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْ أَهْلِي )»، رواه أبو داود، وفي « الحجة » : وإذا خربت القبور فلا بأس بتطيينها، لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مر بقبر ابنه إبراهيم فرأى فيه حجراً سقط منه فسده ثم قال: « مَنْ عَمِلَ عَمَلاً فَلْيُتْقِنَهُ» وفي « التجنيس والمزيد » : تطيين القبور لا بأس به، خلافاً لما يقوله « الكـرخـي» في «مختصره» لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مر بقبر ابنه إبراهيم فرأى فيه حجراً فسده، وقال: « مَنْ عَمِلَ عَمَلاً فَلْيُتْقِنَهُ» انتهى، وكان عصام بن يوسف يطوف حول المدينة يعمر القبور الخربة، ويصلح الطريق والقناطر الخربة، ويتعاهد الضعيف والأرامل ويقوم بأسبابها ، و عن أنس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: صفق الرياح، وقطر الأمطار على قبر المؤمن كَفَّارَةٌ لِذُنُوبِهِ » ) كذا في « التاتارخانية»، (ويُكْرَهُ الدَّفن في البيوتِ، لاختصاصه بالأنبياء عليهمُ الصَّلاةُ والسَّلام) ، قال ( الكمال » : لا يدفن صغير ولا كبير في البيت الذي مات فيه، فإن ذلك خاص بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، بل ينقل إلى مقابر المسلمين، وكذا في « التجنيس». ويُكرهُ الدَّفنُ في الأماكن التي تسمى (الفَسَاقِي) وهي: كبيـت معقود بالبنــاء
And that her grave [of a woman] be covered, not his grave. And earth is poured, and the grave is made hump-shaped, and it is not made square, and building upon it for adornment is prohibited. And they dislike bricks, and some of our mashayikh said: bricks are only disliked if intended for adornment, but if intended to repel harm from beasts or something else, it is not disliked. In al-Khaniyyah: it is disliked if it is next to the deceased, but beyond that there is no harm. In al-Husami: Ismail al-Zahid permitted bricks behind the raw bricks on the side of the niche grave and advised it. In al-Muhit: the mashayikh of Bukhara said: bricks are not disliked in our town due to need because of weak soil, and what is said that the dislike of bricks is due to contact with fire is not correct, because the shroud touches fire and the deceased is washed with hot water. And it is recommended that her grave be covered, i.e., the woman's, because the situation of women is based on concealment until the earth is leveled upon her, and his grave is not covered, because he passed by people who had buried a deceased and spread a cloth over his grave, so he pulled it and said: this is only done for women, except if there is need to repel rain, snow, or heat from those entering the grave, then there is no harm. And earth is poured in the grave for covering, and to this is indicated His saying: to show him how to cover the nakedness of his brother [5:31]. And it is recommended to throw earth upon it, due to the narration that he prayed over a funeral, then came to the grave and threw earth upon it from the side of the head three times. And the grave is made hump-shaped, and it is disliked to increase upon the earth that came out of it, and to make it raised above the ground about a handspan or slightly more, due to what al-Bukhari narrated from Sufyan al-Tammar: I entered the house that contained the grave of the Prophet, and I saw the grave of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and Umar as hump-shaped. And there is no harm in sprinkling water upon it to preserve its earth from erosion, and Abu Yusuf disliked it because it resembles plastering, as in al-Burhan. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: if loss of its trace is feared, then there is no harm in sprinkling water on it without dispute; the dispute is when loss of trace is not feared. It is mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah that it is not disliked, and from Abu Yusuf that it is disliked. And it is not made square nor plastered, due to what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated in al-Athar: Abu Hanifa told us, he said: our teacher narrated to us raising it to the Prophet that he forbade making graves square and plastering them. And building upon it for adornment is prohibited, and it is disliked for consolidation after burial, and there is no harm in writing on it so that its trace is not lost, and it is not treated with disrespect. And burial in houses is disliked, because it is specific to the prophets, peace be upon them, and burial in places called al-fasaqi is disliked.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, expanding rulings related to graves and burial practices. It covers several distinct but related issues. The author begins by discussing the physical construction of the grave: it should be made hump-shaped (musannam) like a camel's hump, not square (murabba'), and building structures on it for adornment is prohibited (haram). The use of bricks (ajur) is generally disliked (makruh), but there are exceptions depending on intention and necessity—if used to prevent beasts or protect the grave, it may be permissible. The text notes differences among Hanafi scholars: some say it is only disliked when near the deceased, others permit it in regions with weak soil where bricks are needed for stability. The argument that bricks are disliked because they are fired in fire is rejected, as the shroud has also been touched by fire and the deceased is washed with hot water. Next, the author addresses covering the grave after burial: it is recommended (mustahabb) to cover the grave of a woman with a cloth, as women are generally concealed, but not a man's grave, based on a hadith where the Prophet pulled a cloth off a man's grave saying such covering is only for women. An exception is made if covering is needed to protect from weather. Then the ruling on sprinkling water on the grave to prevent erosion: it is permitted, though Abu Yusuf disliked it as resembling plastering. The dispute is clarified: when the grave's trace might be lost, there is no disagreement; when not, the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is not disliked. The forbiddance of making graves square and plastering them is emphasized with a hadith narrated by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Building on graves for consolidation after burial is disliked because graves are places of decay, not permanence. Writing on graves to mark them is permitted, and the grave should not be desecrated. Finally, burial in houses is disliked (makruh) because it is specific to prophets; the deceased should be taken to Muslim cemeteries. Burial in places called fasaqi—built chambers with walls and a roof—is also disliked.

Key Terms
تسنیم (tasnīm): Making the grave hump-shaped like the hump of a camel, raised slightly above ground.
تربیع (tarbīʿ): Making the grave square or level with the ground.
تجصیص (tajṣīṣ): Plastering the grave with gypsum or similar material.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on building a structure over a grave for adornment?
A) Sunnah
B) Mubah
C) Haram
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The grave should be hump-shaped (sunnah); squaring, plastering, and building for adornment are prohibited (haram/makruh).

Using Bricks in Graves and Sprinkling Water
Expansion of rulings on bricks and sprinkling water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings on using bricks in grave construction depending on intention and necessity, and state the Hanafi position on sprinkling water on graves.

Core Idea
Bricks are allowed when needed for protection; sprinkling water is permissible to preserve the grave's trace.

This lesson addresses two practical issues: the use of baked bricks (ājur) in grave construction and the sprinkling of water on graves. Both have nuances and intra-Hanafi differences that affect the final fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling on bricks
The text states that bricks are disliked (makruh) by some scholars, but this dislike is conditioned on intention.
The dislike is only when intended for adornment.
2
Examine exceptions
If bricks are used to repel beasts or due to weak soil, they are not disliked.
Mashayikh of Bukhara permitted bricks due to need.
3
Address the fire argument
The argument that bricks are disliked because of contact with fire is rejected because the shroud and hot water also touch fire.
4
Ruling on sprinkling water
Sprinkling water on the grave to preserve its trace is generally permissible. Abu Yusuf disliked it, but the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) permits it.
When loss of trace is feared, there is no dispute.

و أن يُ قبرها، لا قبره. ويُهال التراب، ويُسَنَّمُ القَبرُ ولا يُرَبَّعُ ويَحْرُمُ البناء عليه للزِّينةِ . ويكرهون الآجر، وبعض مشايخنا قالوا: إنما يكره الآجر إذا أُريد به الزينة، أما إذا أُريـد بـه دفـع أذى السباع، أو شيء آخر لا يكره، وفي ( الخانية»: يكره إذا كان مما يلي الميت، أما فيما وراء ذلك فلا بأس به، وفي « الحسامي » وقد رخص إسماعيل الزاهد بالآجر خلف اللبن عـلـى الـلحــد وأوصى به. وفي « المحيط » : قال مشایخ بخارى: لا يكره الآجر في بلدتنا المساس الحاجة إليه لضعف الأراضي، وما قيل: إن كراهة الآجر لمساس النار ليس بصحيح، لأن الكفن مسته النار ويغسل الميت بالماء الحار. (و) يستحب ( أنْ يُسَجَّى) أي يستر (قبرها) :أي: المرأة، لأن مبنى حالهن على الستر إلى أن يسوى عليها الأحد، و (لا) يسجى (قبره)، لأن عليه مر بقوم قد دفنوا ميتاً وبسطوا على قبره ثوباً فجذبه وقال: إنما يصنع هذا بالنساء)، إلا إذا كان لضرورة دفع مطر أو ثلج أو حــر عن الداخلين في القبر، فلا بأس به، ويُهالُ التُّرابُ في القبر للتوارث ستراً له، وإليه وقعت الإشارة بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لِيُرِيَهُ كَيْفَ يُوَارِى سَوْءَةَ أَخِيهِ [للان : ٣١] ويستحب أن يحثي عليه التراب، لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام صلى على جنازة، ثم أتى القبر فحتى عليه التراب من قبل رأسه ثلاثاً). فرأيت قبر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقبر أبي بكر وعمر مسنمة، ولا بأس برش، الماء عليه حفظاً لترابــه عـــن الاندراسه)، وعن أبي يوسف أنه كرهه، لأنه يجري مجرى التطيين، كذا في « البرهان». وفي And that her grave [of a woman] be covered, not his grave. And earth is poured, and the grave is made hump-shaped, and it is not made square, and building upon it for adornment is prohibited. Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, expanding rulings related to graves and burial practices. It covers several distinct but related issues. The author begins by discussing the physical construction of the grave: it should be made hump-shaped (musannam) like a camel's hump, not square (murabba'), and building structures on it for adornment is prohibited (haram). The use of bricks (ajur) is generally disliked (makruh), but there are exceptions depending on intention and necessity—if used to prevent beasts or protect the grave, it may be permissible. The text notes differences among Hanafi scholars: some say it is only disliked when near the deceased, others permit it in regions with weak soil where bricks are needed for stability. The argument that bricks are disliked because they are fired in fire is rejected, as the shroud has also been touched by fire and the deceased is washed with hot water. Next, the author addresses covering the grave after burial: it is recommended (mustahabb) to cover the grave of a woman with a cloth, as women are generally concealed, but not a man's grave, based on a hadith where the Prophet pulled a cloth off a man's grave saying such covering is only for women. An exception is made if covering is needed to protect from weather. Then the ruling on sprinkling water on the grave to prevent erosion: it is permitted, though Abu Yusuf disliked it as resembling plastering. The dispute is clarified: when the grave's trace might be lost, there is no disagreement; when not, the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is not disliked. The forbiddance of making graves square and plastering them is emphasized with a hadith narrated by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Building on graves for consolidation after burial is disliked because graves are places of decay, not permanence. Writing on graves to mark them is permitted, and the grave should not be desecrated. Finally, burial in houses is disliked (makruh) because it is specific to prophets; the deceased should be taken to Muslim cemeteries. Burial in places called fasaqi—built chambers with walls and a roof—is also disliked.

Key Terms
آجر (ājur): Baked bricks used in construction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, which of the following is true about using bricks in graves?
A) Always haram
B) Always makruh
C) Permissible if needed for protection
D) Permissible only if not fired

Key Takeaway
Bricks are permitted for necessity; sprinkling water is permissible, especially to preserve the grave's trace.

Covering the Grave of a Woman and Writing on Graves
Expansion of rulings on covering and writing on graves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on covering the graves of women and men, and on writing on graves.

Core Idea
A woman's grave is covered out of modesty; a man's is not. Writing on graves is allowed to preserve the trace.

This lesson covers two distinct but related practices: covering the grave after burial, especially for women, and writing on graves. Both have specific proofs and intra-Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on covering woman's grave
It is recommended (mustahabb) to cover the grave of a woman with a cloth until the earth is leveled, due to the hadith of the Prophet.
A man's grave is not covered, except for necessity like weather.
2
Understand the exception for necessity
If covering is needed to protect from rain, snow, or heat for those entering the grave, it is permissible.
3
Ruling on writing on graves
Writing on graves is permitted (mubah) to preserve the trace of the grave and avoid disrespect.
Abu Yusuf disliked it, but the relied-upon view is permissibility.
4
Supporting evidence
The hadith of the Prophet marking the grave of Uthman ibn Maz'un with a stone is evidence for marking graves.

And that her grave [of a woman] be covered, not his grave. And earth is poured, and the grave is made hump-shaped, and it is not made square, and building upon it for adornment is prohibited. And they dislike bricks, and some of our mashayikh said: bricks are only disliked if intended for adornment, but if intended to repel harm from beasts or something else, it is not disliked. In al-Khaniyyah: it is disliked if it is next to the deceased, but beyond that there is no harm. In al-Husami: Ismail al-Zahid permitted bricks behind the raw bricks on the side of the niche grave and advised it. In al-Muhit: the mashayikh of Bukhara said: bricks are not disliked in our town due to need because of weak soil, and what is said that the dislike of bricks is due to contact with fire is not correct, because the shroud touches fire and the deceased is washed with hot water. And it is recommended that her grave be covered, i.e., the woman's, because the situation of women is based on concealment until the earth is leveled upon her, and his grave is not covered, because he passed by people who had buried a deceased and spread a cloth over his grave, so he pulled it and said: this is only done for women, except if there is need to repel rain, snow, or heat from those entering the grave, then there is no harm. And earth is poured in the grave for covering, and to this is indicated His saying: to show him how to cover the nakedness of his brother [5:31]. And it is recommended to throw earth upon it, due to the narration that he prayed over a funeral, then came to the grave and threw earth upon it from the side of the head three times. And the grave is made hump-shaped, and it is disliked to increase upon the earth that came out of it, and to make it raised above the ground about a handspan or slightly more, due to what al-Bukhari narrated from Sufyan al-Tammar: I entered the house that contained the grave of the Prophet, and I saw the grave of the Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and Umar as hump-shaped. And there is no harm in sprinkling water upon it to preserve its earth from erosion, and Abu Yusuf disliked it because it resembles plastering, as in al-Burhan. In al-Tatarkhaniyyah: if loss of its trace is feared, then there is no harm in sprinkling water on it without dispute; the dispute is when loss of trace is not feared. It is mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah that it is not disliked, and from Abu Yusuf that it is disliked. And it is not made square nor plastered, due to what Muhammad ibn al-Hasan narrated in al-Athar: Abu Hanifa told us, he said: our teacher narrated to us raising it to the Prophet that he forbade making graves square and plastering them. And building upon it for adornment is prohibited, and it is disliked for consolidation after burial, and there is no harm in writing on it so that its trace is not lost, and it is not treated with disrespect. And burial in houses is disliked, because it is specific to the prophets, peace be upon them, and burial in places called al-fasaqi is disliked.

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary (sharh) on Nur al-Idah, expanding rulings related to graves and burial practices. It covers several distinct but related issues. The author begins by discussing the physical construction of the grave: it should be made hump-shaped (musannam) like a camel's hump, not square (murabba'), and building structures on it for adornment is prohibited (haram). The use of bricks (ajur) is generally disliked (makruh), but there are exceptions depending on intention and necessity—if used to prevent beasts or protect the grave, it may be permissible. Next, the author addresses covering the grave after burial: it is recommended (mustahabb) to cover the grave of a woman with a cloth, as women are generally concealed, but not a man's grave, based on a hadith where the Prophet pulled a cloth off a man's grave saying such covering is only for women. An exception is made if covering is needed to protect from weather. Then the ruling on sprinkling water on the grave to prevent erosion: it is permitted, though Abu Yusuf disliked it as resembling plastering. The dispute is clarified: when the grave's trace might be lost, there is no disagreement; when not, the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that it is not disliked. فساقی (fasāqī): Built chambers with walls and a roof, like a small room.
