Rulings on Mourning: Sitting, Gatherings, and Food
Rulings on mourning practices: sitting, gatherings, and hospitality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on mourning gatherings and the proper conduct for the bereaved, and distinguish between disliked and recommended practices.

Core Idea
In mourning, serving the bereaved is sunnah; hospitality by the bereaved is disliked.

After a death, how should a Muslim community respond? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: the bereaved should not be burdened with hosting, and neighbors should step in with food and support. This lesson unpacks the rulings on sitting in mourning, gathering at the bereaved's home, and preparing food, drawing from the Qur'anic etiquette and prophetic example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, list each mourning practice mentioned (sitting for three days, sitting longer, gathering at the house, hospitality by the bereaved, neighbors preparing food) and state the hukm level for each.
Note that the ruling changes depending on the duration and who performs the act.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidence cited: from Jarir ibn Abdullah (gathering and food preparation counted as wailing) and the hadith 'no 'aqr in Islam'.
These ahadith are the proofs for the disliked ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadiths prove the ruling: the Companions considered such gatherings and food akin to wailing, which is forbidden; thus hospitality by the bereaved becomes disliked.
The analogy is that any action resembling pre-Islamic wailing is prohibited.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Compare the classical permissive view (sitting three days allowed, khilaf al-awla) with the later mutakhkhirin position that gatherings and sitting are disliked.
The text gives preference to the stricter view as the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling: the bereaved should not sit to receive condolences, neighbors should provide food, and hospitality by the bereaved is disliked.
This is the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: يجوز الجلوس للمصيبة ثلاثة أيام وهو خلاف الأولى، ويكره أكثر منها، وترك الجلوس أحسن، وقال كثير من متأخري أئمتنا رحمهم الله يكره الاجتماع عند صاحب البيت، ويكره له الجلوس في بيته حتى يأتي إليه من يعزي، بل إذا فرغ ورجع الناس من الدفن فليتفرقوا، ويشتغل الناس بأمورهم، وصاحب الميت بأمره انتهى. وفي «التجنيس»: يكره الجلوس على باب الدار للمصيبة، فإن ذلك عمل أهل الجاهلية، ونهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن ذلك، ويكره في المسجد، وتكره الضيافة من أهل الميت؛ لأنها شرعت في السرور لا في الشرور، وهي بدعة مستقبحة، روى الإمام أحمد وابن ماجه بإسناد صحيح عن جرير بن عبد الله، قال: كنا نعد الاجتماع إلى أهل الميت وصنعهم الطعام من النياحة، وقال الزيلعي: وعن أنس قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا عقر في الإسلام» وهو الذي كان يعقر عند القبر ببقرة أو شاة انتهى. ويستحب للجيران وأهل الميت من الأقرباء الأباعد تهيئة طعام لأهل الميت، يشبعهم يومهم وليلتهم، لقوله: (اصنعوا لآل جعفر طعامًا فقد جاءهم ما يشغلهم). حسنه الترمذي وصححه الحاكم، ويلح عليهم في الأكل، لأن الحزن يمنعهم فيضعفهم.
Continuation: It is permissible to sit (in mourning) for the deceased for three days, but it is not the best; more than that is disliked, and leaving the sitting (altogether) is better. Many of our later imams (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is disliked to gather at the house of the bereaved, and it is disliked for him to sit in his house until people come to console him. Rather, when the burial is finished and people return, they should disperse, and people should attend to their own affairs, and the bereaved to his own matter—end. In al-Tajnis: It is disliked to sit at the door of the house for mourning, for that is the practice of the people of ignorance (Jahiliyyah), and the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade that. It is disliked in the mosque. Hospitality from the family of the deceased is disliked, because it is prescribed for joys, not sorrows, and it is a reprehensible innovation. Imam Ahmad and Ibn Majah narrated with a sound chain from Jarir ibn Abdullah: He said, 'We used to consider gathering with the family of the deceased and their preparing food as part of wailing (niyahah).' Al-Zayla'i said: And from Anas, he (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no 'aqr in Islam' – and 'aqr is (the practice of) slaughtering a cow or sheep at the grave – end. It is recommended for the neighbors and distant relatives of the deceased to prepare food for the family of the deceased, to satisfy them for their day and night, because of his saying: 'Make food for the family of Ja'far, for there has come to them that which occupies them.' al-Tirmidhi classified it as good (hasan) and al-Hakim as authentic (sahih). And they should urge them to eat, because grief prevents them and weakens them.
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on mourning practices after a death, drawn from the Hanafi school. It begins with a permissive ruling: sitting in mourning for three days is allowed, but it is not the preferred practice; refraining from sitting altogether is better. However, the later Hanafi scholars take a stricter view, stating that gathering at the bereaved's house is disliked, and the bereaved should not sit waiting for condolences; after burial, people should leave. The text then cites al-Tajnis, emphasizing that sitting at the door for mourning is a Jahili custom and is explicitly forbidden by the Prophet. Hospitality (making food for visitors) by the bereaved family is also disliked, as it is an innovation; a hadith from Jarir shows that the Companions considered such gatherings and food preparation akin to wailing. Instead, neighbors and distant relatives should prepare food for the bereaved, based on the Prophet's instruction to the family of Ja'far. This reverses the normal practice: the bereaved should be served, not serve others.

Key Terms
الجلوس للمصيبة (al-julus li al-musibah): Sitting (by the bereaved or others) to receive condolences, i.e., mourning gatherings.
الضيافة (al-diyafah): Hospitality (making food) from the bereaved family for those who come to console.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the bereaved family preparing food for those who visit to console them?
A) Mustahabb (recommended)
B) Mubah (permissible)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the bereaved should not host visitors or prepare food; neighbors and relatives should provide for them.

The Recommendation of Ta'ziyah (Consoling the Bereaved)
Rulings on the reward and method of consoling the bereaved

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'ziyah, identify the hadith evidence, and apply the rule that ta'ziyah is recommended once.

Core Idea
Ta'ziyah is a recommended act of consolation, supported by hadith, and should be performed only once.

Ta'ziyah, or consoling the bereaved after a death, is a commendable act in the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the ruling from the matn of Nur al-Idah, which states it is mustahabb and provides hadith evidence. You will also learn the important condition that it should not be repeated, a nuance often overlooked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, locate the legal act being discussed: ta'ziyah (consoling). The text states it is 'mustahabb' (recommended). Understand that this is a hukm taklifi at the level of recommendation, not obligation.
The Arabic 'tustahabb' explicitly places it in the mustahabb/sunnah category.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites three hadiths. Identify them: the promise of clothing in Paradise, reward equal to the afflicted, and being clothed with two garments. These are ahad hadith, giving zanni thubut and dalala.
The hadiths are mentioned but not fully quoted; the commentator provides the source as Fath al-Qadir.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each hadith indicates recommendation. The promise of reward in Paradise (e.g., garments) is not a threat of punishment but a motivation, which corresponds to the level of mandub (recommended).
In Hanafi usul, the absence of a threat (wa'id) for omission indicates it is not wajib.
4
Identify the additional ruling
The text also states 'la yanbaghi' (it is not appropriate) to console again after once. This is a ruling of karahah tanzihiyyah (disliked but not prohibited). Trace this to a transmission from Abu Hanifa via al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
This shows that even recommended acts have limits; excess can be makruh.
5
Apply the ruling
Now apply: for a Hanafi, ta'ziyah is meritorious but should be done once. If someone consoles repeatedly, it is makruh tanzihan. Consider the condition for women: it is only recommended if they do not cause fitnah.
This condition reflects the principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتستحب التعزية للرجال والنساء اللاتي لا يفتن لقوله: «من عزى أخاه بمصيبة كساه الله من حلل الكرامة يوم القيامة» وقوله: «من عزى مصابًا فله مثل أجره» وقوله: «من عزى تكلَى كسي بردين في الجنة» كذا في «فتح القدير»، ولا ينبغي لمن عزى مرة أن يعزي مرة أخرى، رواه الحسن عن أبي حنيفة في التاتارخانية) (والله أعلم).
And ta'ziyah (consoling) is recommended for men and for women who do not cause temptation, because of his saying: 'Whoever consoles his brother in a calamity, Allah will clothe him with garments of honor on the Day of Resurrection' and his saying: 'Whoever consoles an afflicted person, he will have a reward like his' and his saying: 'Whoever consoles (someone) will be clothed with two garments in Paradise.' Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is not appropriate for one who has consoled once to console again; narrated by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifah in al-Tatarikhaniyyah (and Allah knows best).
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on ta'ziyah, which is the act of consoling the bereaved after a death. The text states that it is recommended (mustahabb) for both men and women, with the condition for women that they do not cause fitnah (temptation). The proof comes from three hadiths that promise great rewards for consoling: clothing of honor in Paradise, a reward equal to the afflicted, and garments in Paradise. These hadiths are cited as recorded in Fath al-Qadir. Additionally, consoling should be done only once; repeating it is disapproved (la yanbaghi). This ruling is attributed to al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's transmission from Abu Hanifah, as found in al-Tatarikhaniyyah. The passage underscores that ta'ziyah is a meritorious act but should not become an extended practice.

Key Terms
التعزية (al-ta'ziyah): Consoling the bereaved, encouraging patience, and praying for the deceased.
مستحب (mustahabb): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; its performance is rewarded and its omission is not sinful.
لا ينبغي (la yanbaghi): It is not appropriate; used here to indicate karahah tanzihiyyah (disliked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many times should ta'ziyah (consoling) be performed?
A) As many times as needed
B) Once
C) Three times
D) Seven times

Key Takeaway
Ta'ziyah is a recommended act of consolation, supported by ahad hadith, and must be performed only once to avoid disapproval.

The Hanafi Ruling on Ta'ziyah (Condolence)
Concludes discussion on ta'ziyah with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'ziyah and identify the conditions that affect its recommendation.

Core Idea
Ta'ziyah is recommended once for men and for women free from fitnah.

This passage concludes the discussion on ta'ziyah by stating its ruling and supporting it with prophetic hadiths. The author clarifies that condolences are recommended (mustahabb) for both men and women, provided that women's participation does not lead to fitnah (temptation). The passage also emphasizes that offering condolences should not be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what ta'ziyah is and what legal category it falls under (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.).
The text says 'tustahabb' (it is recommended).
2
Determine the conditions
Note the condition about women: only those who do not cause fitnah. Also note the limitation: not to be repeated.
Fitnah refers to temptation or social turmoil.
3
Examine the dalil
The author cites three hadiths promising reward. Identify the type of proof and how it indicates recommendation.
Ahad hadiths provide zanni evidence, sufficient for mustahabb.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a practical situation, e.g., a death in the community. Decide who may offer condolences and how many times.
Once is sufficient; repeating is discouraged.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on ta'ziyah (condolence). The author declares that Allah inspires patience and compensates reward. He then rules that ta'ziyah is mustahabb (recommended) for both men and women, provided they do not cause fitnah (temptation or turmoil). This is supported by three hadiths promising great rewards: being clothed with garments of honor on the Day of Resurrection, receiving a reward equal to the afflicted person, and being given two garments in Paradise. The author quotes from Fath al-Qadir. He then adds a note that ta'ziyah should not be repeated more than once, based on a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifah as recorded in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms

الفتنة (al-fitnah): Temptation or turmoil, especially due to intermingling of genders.

Visiting Graves: Ruling and Recommended Recitations
Opens chapter on visiting graves, stating ruling and recommended recitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on visiting graves for men and women, cite the proof for reciting Ya-Sin, and describe the Sunnah method of visitation.

Core Idea
Visiting graves is recommended for both genders; the Sunnah is to stand and recite Ya-Sin.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on visiting graves. The author opens the chapter by stating that it is recommended (mandub) for both men and women, according to the correct view. He then addresses a conflicting opinion that it is forbidden for women and resolves it by citing later authorities. Finally, he presents the prophetic example of visiting standing and the virtue of reciting Surah Ya-Sin, supported by multiple hadiths.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the legal ruling (mandub) and who it applies to (men and women). Note that the text says 'ala al-ashahh' (on the correct view), indicating a preferred position.
The ruling is not wajib or haram, but recommended.
2
Analyze the ikhtilaf on women
Observe the opposing view from al-Tatarkhaniyyah that visiting graves is forbidden for women. Then evaluate the tarjih: the author sides with al-Bahr and al-Fath that the permission is established for both.
The harsh statement from the judge is presented as an extreme view, not the relied-upon position.
3
Examine the dalil for recitation
Look at the hadith cited: 'Whoever enters the graveyards and recites Ya-Sin, Allah lightens the punishment for them...'. Identify the reward and how it proves merit.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut (ahad) but sufficient for mandub.
4
Summarize the Sunnah method
Extract the recommended practice: visit standing, make the prophetic supplication, and recite Ya-Sin (or al-Ikhlas eleven times).
The Sunnah method is to stand and face the graves.

Chapter on Visiting Graves: Its visitation is recommended for men and women, according to the correct view. And it is recommended to recite Ya-Sin because it has been reported that: 'Whoever enters the graveyards and recites Ya-Sin, Allah lightens the punishment for them on that day, and he will have rewards equal to the number of (the dead) in them.' And it was said: It is forbidden for women. The judge was asked about the permissibility of women going out to the graveyards and said: Do not ask about permissibility and corruption in such a matter; rather ask about the amount of curse that will befall her therein. Know that every time she intends to go out, she is under the curse of Allah and His angels. When she goes out, she is surrounded by devils from every side. When she comes to the graves, the soul of the dead curses her. When she returns, she is under the curse of Allah — as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, from Kifayat al-Sha'bi. And it is said in al-Bahr: The more correct view is that permission is established for men and women, so it is recommended for them as well, according to the correct view. And the Sunnah is to visit standing, and to make supplication standing, as the Messenger of Allah used to do when going out to al-Baqi', saying: 'Peace be upon you, abode of a believing people. Indeed we, Allah willing, will join you. I ask Allah for well-being for me and for you' — as in al-Fath. And it is recommended for the visitor to recite Surah Ya-Sin because it has been reported that: 'Whoever enters the graveyards and recites Ya-Sin, Allah lightens the punishment for them on that day' — as in al-Bahr. And it raises (the punishment) from the Muslims, then it does not return to them, as some gnostics have stated. Likewise on Friday, the punishment is lifted from the people of the grave. And he (the reciter) will have rewards equal to the number of (the dead) in them. And in al-Burhan: The Prophet said: 'Recite Ya-Sin to your dead' — narrated by Abu Dawud. And the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever passes by the graveyards and recites Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad eleven times, then gifts its reward to the dead, he will be given a reward equal to the number of the dead.' And Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from al-Hasan that he said: 'Whoever enters the graveyards and says: O Allah...'

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on visiting graves (ziyarat al-qubur). The author states that visiting graves is mandub (recommended) for both men and women according to the correct view. He then presents an opposing view that it is haram for women, quoting a harsh statement from a judge about curses. However, he cites al-Bahr to affirm that the correct position is that permission is established for both genders and it is recommended. The Sunnah method is to visit standing, and to make the supplication as taught by the Prophet. The author highly recommends reciting Surah Ya-Sin, citing multiple hadiths: it lightens punishment, raises punishment from the dead, and the reciter receives rewards equal to the number of the dead. Additional recitations include Surah al-Ikhlas eleven times, and a supplication taught by al-Hasan. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on visiting graves as a recommended act with specific etiquettes and rewards.

Key Terms
زيارة القبور (ziyarat al-qubur): Visiting graves, typically of Muslims, for remembrance of death and supplication for the dead.
ندب (nudiba): An act that is recommended (mandub) – doing it is rewarded, not doing it is not sinful.

Conditions for a Valid Vow (Nadhr) to be Binding
Defines the three conditions for a vow to be binding and gives examples of invalid vows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid vow and apply them to determine whether a given vowed act is binding.

Core Idea
A vow binds only if the act is a primary worship, not already obligatory, and of a type wajib in essence.

In this passage, the author explains the legal framework for when a vow (nadhr) creates a binding obligation. Understanding these conditions is essential because many people mistakenly assume any good deed can be vowed. The author uses examples like wudu, Quran recitation, and visiting the sick to illustrate which vows are valid and which are not. We will dissect each condition and see how they apply to real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the vow (nadhr) and the obligation to fulfill it. The ruling is that fulfilling a valid vow is wajib.
The general obligation is established by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 22:29 and a hadith from Bukhari: 'Whoever vows to obey Allah, let him obey Him...' Plus consensus.
The hadith is ahad in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fal-yuti'hu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The prohibition 'fala ya'sihi' shows sinful vows are not to be fulfilled.
This establishes the basic rule: vows of obedience must be fulfilled; vows of disobedience must not.
4
Identify the three conditions for binding
The text lists three conditions: (1) the type must be wajib in origin, (2) the act must be intended for itself (maqsud li-dhatihi), (3) it must not already be wajib by Allah's command.
A fourth condition (non-impossibility) is also mentioned.
5
Apply the conditions to the examples and note the ikhtilaf
Wudu fails condition 2 (means to prayer, not an end). Quran recitation may fail condition 1 (type not wajib) or condition 2. Sajdat al-tilawa fails condition 3 (already wajib). Visiting the sick fails condition 1 (type not wajib). An alternate narration from Abu Hanifa holds that general visits are binding.
The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) treats all these as invalid vows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يلزم الوفاء به من منذور الصوم والصلاة وغيرهما إذا نَذَرَ شيئاً لزمه الوفاء به، إذا اجتمع فيه ثلاثة شروط: أن يكون من جنسه واجب، وأن يكون مقصوداً، وأن يكون ليس واجباً، فلا يلزم الوضوء بنذره ولا سجدة التلاوة ولا عيادة المريض. قال في المصباح: نذرت كذا نذراً، من باب ضرب، وفي لغة قتل. إذا نَذَرَ شيئاً من القربات لَزِمَهُ الوفاء به لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيُوفُوا نُذُورَهُمْ﴾ [الحج: ۲۹] وقوله: «مَنْ نَذَرَ أَنْ يُطِيعَ الله فَلْيُطِعْهُ، ومَنْ نَذَرَ أَنْ يَعْصِيَ الله فَلا يَعْصِهِ» رواه البخاري، والإجماع على وجوب الإيفاء به. وبين شرط لزوم المنذور بقوله: إذا اجتمع فيه ثلاثة شروط: أحدها: أن يكون من جنسه واجب بأصله، وإن حرم ارتكابه لوصفه، كصوم يوم النحر. والثاني: أن يكون مقصوداً لذاته لا لغيره كالوضوء. والثالث: أن يكون ليس واجباً قبل نذره بإيجاب الله تعالى، كالصلوات الخمس والوتر. وقد زيد شرط رابع: أن لا يكون المنذور محالاً، كقوله: علي صوم أمس اليوم إذ لا يلزمه، وكذا لو قال: أمس وكان قوله بعد الزوال كما في الخانية. ثم فرع على ذلك بقوله: فلا يلزم الوضوء بنذره ولا قراءة القرآن؛ لكون الوضوء ليس مقصوداً لذاته؛ لأنه شرط لغيره كحل الصلاة، ولا سجدة التلاوة لأنها واجبة بإيجاب الشارع، ولا عيادة المريض إذ ليس من جنسه واجب. وإيجاب العبد معتبر بإيجاب الله تعالى، إذ له الاتباع لا الابتداع، وهذا في ظاهر الرواية. وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة قال: إن نذر أن يعود مريضاً اليوم صح نذره، وإن نذر أن يعود فلاناً لا يلزمه شيء؛ لأن عيادة المريض قربة شرعاً قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «عَائِدُ المَرِيضِ عَلَى مَخَارِفِ الجنَّةِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ»، وعيادة فلان بعينه، لا يكون معنى القربة فيه مقصوداً للناذر، بل مراعاة حق فلان، فلا يصح التزامه بالنذر. وفي ظاهر الرواية: عيادة المريض وتشييع الجنازة، وإن كان فيه معنى حق الله تعالى، فالمقصود حق المريض والميت.
Chapter: What is necessary to fulfill from vowed fasting, prayer, and other acts. If one vows something, fulfillment becomes binding, provided three conditions are met: that its type is obligatory in essence, that it is intended for itself, and that it is not already obligatory. So wudu is not binding by vowing it, nor is prostration of recitation, nor visiting the sick. It says in al-Misbah: 'I vowed such and such a vow,' from the pattern of daraba, and in another language qatala. If one vows something from acts of devotion, fulfillment is binding upon him due to the verse: 'And let them fulfill their vows' [22:29] and his saying: 'Whoever vows to obey Allah, let him obey Him, and whoever vows to disobey Allah, let him not disobey Him.' The obligation of fulfillment is established by consensus. He then explained the conditions for the binding of the vowed act: when three conditions are met: first, that its type is obligatory in its origin, even if its description is prohibited, like fasting on the day of Nahr. Second, that it is intended for its own sake, not for something else, like wudu. Third, that it is not already obligatory by Allah's decree, like the five prayers and witr. A fourth condition has been added: that the vowed act not be impossible, like saying: 'I owe fasting yesterday,' which is not binding, similarly if he said 'yesterday' after noon as in al-Khaniyyah. Then he branched from that: wudu is not binding by vowing it, nor recitation of Quran, because wudu is not intended for its own sake; it is a condition for something else like permitting prayer. Nor prostration of recitation because it is obligatory by the Lawgiver. Nor visiting the sick because its type is not obligatory. The obligation imposed by the slave is considered in light of Allah's imposition, for he has permission to follow, not to innovate. This is in Zahir al-Riwayah. In another narration from Abu Hanifa, he said: If one vows to visit a sick person today, his vow is valid; if he vows to visit a specific person, nothing is binding, because visiting the sick is a legislated act of devotion. The Prophet said: 'The visitor of the sick remains on the gardens of Paradise until he returns.' Visiting a specific person does not have the meaning of devotion intended by the vower; rather it is observing the right of that person, so its commitment by vow is not valid. In Zahir al-Riwayah: visiting the sick and following the funeral, although they contain the meaning of Allah's right, the intended purpose is the right of the sick person and the deceased.
Source pages p. 671

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on the conditions for a vow (nadhr) to be binding in Hanafi law. It begins with the general rule: if one vows something from acts of worship, fulfillment is obligatory, citing the Quranic verse (22:29) and a hadith from Bukhari. The text then lays out three conditions for the vow to be binding: (1) the vowed act must be of a type that is wajib in its original essence (asl), even if its specific description is prohibited (e.g., fasting on the day of Nahr is prohibited but the type of fasting is wajib in essence); (2) the act must be intended for its own sake (maqsud li-dhatihi), not as a means to something else (e.g., wudu is not intended for itself but as a condition for prayer); (3) the act must not already be wajib by Allah's command (e.g., the five daily prayers and witr are already obligatory, so vowing them is meaningless). A fourth condition mentioned is that the act must not be impossible (e.g., fasting yesterday). The text then applies these conditions to specific examples: vowing to perform wudu, recite Quran, perform prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa), or visit the sick – none of these are binding by vow. For wudu and Quran recitation, they are not maqsud li-dhatihi; for sajdat al-tilawa, it is already wajib; for visiting the sick, its type is not wajib in origin. The passage then mentions an alternate narration from Abu Hanifa: if one vows to visit a sick person in general, the vow is valid because it is a legislated act of devotion; but if he vows to visit a specific person (like Zayd), the vow is not binding because the intention is the right of that person, not devotion. However, the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that even general visiting of the sick is not binding by vow because the primary purpose is the right of the sick person, not an act of devotion intended for itself.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow, a commitment to perform an act of worship that is not already obligatory, made conditional or unconditional.
مقصود لذاته (maqsud li-dhatihi): The act is intended for its own sake, i.e., it is a primary act of worship, not a means to another act.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The primary transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, collected in the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid condition for a vow to be binding according to the text?
A) The vowed act must be haram.
B) The vowed act must be of a type that is obligatory in its essence, even if the specific instance is prohibited.
C) The vowed act must be mubah (permissible).
D) The vowed act must be performed immediately.

Key Takeaway
A vow is only binding if the vowed act is a primary act of worship of a type that is wajib in essence, not already obligatory, and not impossible.

Conditions for a Binding Vow (Nadhr) in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof: three conditions for binding vows and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a binding vow and apply them to determine whether specific vowed acts (e.g., wudu, visiting the sick) become binding.

Core Idea
A vow binds only if its kind is wajib, it is intended for itself, and it is not already obligatory.

Not every vow becomes legally binding. The Hanafi school sets precise conditions to prevent frivolous commitments and to align with the Shariah's categories of obligation. This lesson unpacks those conditions and their application to common examples like vowing to pray, fast, or visit the sick.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
List the three conditions stated by the author for a vow to be binding: (1) the vowed act's kind must be wajib (obligatory) in origin, (2) the act must be intended for itself (not a means to another act), and (3) the act must not already be obligatory by Allah's command before the vow.
2
Understand the rationale for each condition
Explain why each condition is necessary: Condition 1 ensures the vow is an act of obedience; Condition 2 ensures the act is an end in itself, not a mere means; Condition 3 prevents vowing something already required, as the vow adds nothing.
The fourth condition about impossibility is added from other Hanafi sources.
3
Apply conditions to the examples given
Take the examples: wudu, prostration of recitation, visiting the sick. For each, determine which condition fails and why. For wudu, condition 2 fails (it is a means to prayer). For prostration of recitation, condition 3 fails (it is already wajib). For visiting the sick, condition 1 fails (its kind is mandub, not wajib).
Note the nuance: even if the kind is wajib, a specific instance might be prohibited (e.g., fasting on Eid).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on visiting the sick
Contrast the Zahir al-Riwayah position (visiting the sick never binds via vow) with Abu Hanifa's other narration (binds if general vow to visit any sick person). Understand the reasoning: the former emphasizes the right of the sick person over the act of worship; the latter emphasizes the qurbah element.
The mufta bihi is Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Connect to the proofs
The author cites Quran 22:29 and a hadith. The imperative 'ليوفوا' indicates obligation (wujub) but is general; the conditions specify its application. The hadith reinforces that vows must be acts of obedience.
The proof is from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma.

(و) الثالث: (أنْ يَكُونَ ليس واجباً) قبل نذره بإيجاب الله تعالى، كالصلوات الخمس والوتر، وقد زيد شرط رابع : أن لا يكون المنذور محالاً، كقوله: علي صوم أمس اليوم إذ لا يلزمه، وكذا لو قال: أمس وكان قوله بعد الزوال كما في الخانية ، ثم فرع على ذلك بقوله: (فلا يلزم الوضوء بنذرِهِ) ولا قراءة القرآن؛ لكون الوضوء ليس مقصود لذاته؛ لأنه شرط لغيره كحل الصلاة، ولا سجدة التلاوة) لأنها واجبة بإيجاب الشارع، (ولا عيادة المريض) إذ ليس من جنسه واجب، وإيجاب العبد معتبر بإيجاب الله تعالى، إذ له الاتباع لا الابتداع، وهذا في ظاهر الراوية. وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة قال: إن نذر أن يعود مريضاً اليوم صح نذره، وإن نذر أن يعود فلاناً لا يلزمه شيء؛ لأن عيادة المريض قربة شرعاً قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « عَائِدُ المَرِيضِ عَلَى مَخَارِف الجَنَّةِ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ ) (۳)، وعيادة فلان بعينه، لا يكون معنى القربة فيه مقصوداً للناذر ، بل مراعاة حق فلان، فلا يصح التزامه بالنذر. وفي ظاهر الرواية: عيادة المريض وتشييع الجنازة، وإن كان فيه معنى حق الله تعالى، فالمقصود حق المريض والميت
Chapter of what is obligatory to fulfill from vowed fasts, prayers, and others. If one vows something, fulfilling it becomes obligatory, when three conditions are met: that its kind is obligatory (in origin), that it is intended for itself, and that it is not already obligatory. So wudu is not obligated by vowing it, nor the prostration of recitation, nor visiting the sick. (2) Chapter... He said in al-Misbah: 'nadhartu kadha nadhran' from the paradigm daraba, and in a language qatala, end. (If one vows something) from acts of worship (fulfilling it becomes obligatory) due to His statement: 'Let them fulfill their vows' [al-Hajj 29] and his statement: 'Whoever vows to obey Allah, let him obey Him, and whoever vows to disobey Allah, let him not disobey Him' narrated by al-Bukhari, and consensus on the obligation of fulfilling it, and by it those who say it is obligatory argue, and he explained the condition for the vowed thing's binding nature by his saying: (when three conditions are met in it) i.e., the vowed thing: one: that its kind is obligatory in origin, even if performing it is prohibited due to a description, like fasting the day of sacrifice; second: that it is intended for itself not for something else like wudu; third: that it is not obligatory before his vow by Allah's command, like the five prayers and witr. A fourth condition is added: that the vowed thing not be impossible, like saying: 'upon me is fasting yesterday today' as it is not binding, and similarly if he said 'yesterday' and his statement was after noon as in al-Khaniyah. Then he branched from that by his saying: (so wudu is not obligated by his vow) nor reciting the Quran because wudu is not intended for itself; it is a condition for something else like solving prayer; nor the prostration of recitation because it is obligatory by the Lawgiver's command; (nor visiting the sick) because its kind is not obligatory, and the servant's making obligatory is considered by Allah's making obligatory; he has following, not innovating. This is in the apparent narration. And in a narration from Abu Hanifa, he said: If he vows to visit a sick person today, his vow is valid; if he vows to visit so-and-so, nothing is binding on him because visiting the sick is legally an act of worship – the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The visitor of the sick is on the fruits of Paradise until he returns' – and visiting a specific person, the meaning of worship is not intended by the vow, rather it is observing the right of so-and-so, so his undertaking by vow is not valid. In the apparent narration: visiting the sick and accompanying the funeral, even if there is the meaning of Allah's right in them, the purpose is the right of the sick and the deceased.
Source pages p. 671

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the conditions for a binding vow in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating the chapter heading, then presents the general rule: if one vows something, fulfilling it is obligatory, but only if three conditions are met. The first condition is that the kind of act vowed must be from a category that is wajib (obligatory) in its origin, even if performing it at that time might be prohibited due to a secondary description (e.g., fasting on the day of Sacrifice is originally wajib, but that specific day is prohibited). Second, the act must be intended for itself (maqsud li-dhatihi), not as a means to something else, like wudu which is only a condition for prayer. Third, the act must not already be obligatory by Allah's command before the vow, such as the five daily prayers and witr. The author adds a fourth condition from other sources: the vow must not be impossible, like vowing to fast yesterday. He then gives examples of acts that do not become binding when vowed: wudu, reciting Quran, prostration of recitation, and visiting the sick. For each, he explains why the condition fails. Finally, he presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding visiting the sick: in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), visiting the sick is not binding because it is not from a category that is wajib per se; but a narration from Abu Hanifa distinguishes between vowing to visit a sick person generally (valid) vs. vowing to visit a specific person (invalid). This shows the nuance in Hanafi fiqh regarding intentions and the nature of the act.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow; an undertaking to perform an act of worship for Allah, which becomes wajib to fulfill if conditions are met.
واجب (wajib): An act that is obligatory by a zanni evidence; in the context of vows, it refers to acts that are obligatory in their original category (e.g., fasting from the category of fasting).
مقصوداً لذاته (maqsudan li-dhatihi): Intended for its own sake; an act that is an end in itself, not a means to another act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Vowing to perform wudu before each prayer.
B) Vowing to visit a sick friend.
C) Vowing to fast on a day that is not already obligatory.
D) Vowing to recite the Qur'an after every prayer.

Key Takeaway
A vow is only binding if the vowed act belongs to a wajib category, is an end in itself, and is not already obligatory by Shariah.

Conditional Vows: When Does a Vow Become Binding?
Ruling on conditional vows with proof from hadith and intra-Hanafi discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional vows and apply it to scenarios, distinguishing between valid and invalid fulfillment, and identify when a vague vow is treated as an oath.

Core Idea
A conditional vow is only fulfilled after the condition occurs; performing before is not accepted.

Vows (nadhur) are serious commitments to Allah. When a vow is made conditional on a future event, the obligation does not arise until that event occurs. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidence, and related issues such as performing the vow before the condition, the virtue of prayer in sacred mosques, and the treatment of vague vows that may be considered oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vow and its condition
Read the source text and find the example: 'If Zayd comes, upon me for Allah is that I give charity a certain amount.' Recognize that the vow is suspended (mu'allaq) on the condition of Zayd's arrival.
The condition can be any future event; the vow becomes binding only after its occurrence.
2
Determine when fulfillment is valid
The text states that performing the vowed act before the condition exists is not acceptable as fulfillment. The reason: the obligation (wujub) arises only after the condition is met. Therefore, the act must be performed after the condition.
This distinguishes conditional vows from immediate vows, where fulfillment is valid anytime.
3
Understand the digression on mosque virtues
The passage cites hadith about the superiority of prayer in the Prophet's Mosque and the Sacred Mosque. This is used to illustrate a related scenario: if a woman vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque, according to Imam Zufar, praying in the darkest part of her house (the best place for a woman) suffices because it is more virtuous.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the main view is not fully detailed here.
4
Distinguish between vows and oaths
The text explains that the formula of a vow can also be intended as an oath. If the vower has no specific intention, it is treated as a vow by consensus. If he intends an oath, it becomes an oath requiring kaffarah if broken. If both are intended, both obligations apply: qada' for the vow and kaffarah for the oath.
Understanding intention (niyyah) is crucial in these cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن عَلْقَ النَّذَرَ بشرط لا يُجزتُهُ عنه ما فعله قبل وجودِ شَرْطِهِ
صَلَاةٍ فِي بَيْتِ المَقْدِسِ، وَصَلَاةٌ فِي المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ تَعْدِلُ أَلْفَ صَلاةٍ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا ) قلت: وحكم مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يختص بالبقعة التي كانت مسجداً في زمنه ؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: (صَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، وَلَو مَدْ إلَى صَنْعَاءَ بِألْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيمَا سِوَاهُ مِنَ المَسَاجِدِ إِلا المَسْجِدِ الحَرَام ) قاله النسائي في أخبار المدينة، كذا في « ترتيب المقاصد الحسنة للسخاوي»، وروى البزار بإسناد صحيح أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: صَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيْمَا سِوَاهُ، إِلا المَسْجِدَ الحَرَامَ، فَإِنَّهُ يَزِيْدُ عَلَيْهِ مَائَةَ أَلْفِ صَلَاةٍ » (۳) وفي حديث: « وَشَهْرُ رَمَضَانَ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ شَهْرٍ، فِيْمَا سِوَاهُ إِلَّا المَسْجِدِ الحرام » رواه البيهقي، وهذا دليل لأهل السنة والجماعة، أن لبعض الأمكنة فضيلة على بعض، وكذا الأزمنة، ولما سئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل صلاة المرأة فقال: « في أشَدَّ مَكانٍ في بيتها ظلمة ، فـعـلـى هـذا ينبغي أنها إذا التزمت الصلاة في المسجد الحرام بالنذر، فصلت في أشد مكان في بيتها ظلمة، أن تخرج عن موجب نذرها، على ما يقوله زفر والدليل مبسوط في محله. (وإنْ عَلَّقَ) الناذر (النَّدْرَ بشرط) كقوله: إن قدم زيد فلله علي أن أتصدق بكذا، ( لا يُجْزِتُهُ عنه ما فعله قبل وجودِ شَرْطِهِ))؛ لأن المعلق بالشرط عدم قبل وجوده، وإنما يجوز الأداء بعد وجود السبب الذي علق بالنذر به.
بقي ما لو وجد الشرط هل يتعين الزمان والمكان والفقير والدرهم؟ والظاهر نعم لما في التنوير. ثم إن عقله بشرط يريده كإن قدم غائبي يوفي إن وجد ا.هـ فإنه لا يكون موفياً إلا إذا كان على الوجه المذكور في نذره. [ تتمة ] النذر لا يدخل تحت الحكم ولو بعتق رقبة في ملكه نذر أن يذبح ولده فعليه شاة لقصة الخليل علام. نذر أن يتصدق بعشرة دراهم من الخبز فتصدق بغيره جاز إن ساوى العشرة كتصدقه بثمنه. قال علي نذر ولم يزد عليه ولا نية له فعليه كفارة يمين، فإن وصل به المشيئة بطل لأنها تبطل كل ما تعلق بالقول عبادة أو معاملة. قال إن ذهبت هذه العلة فعلي كذا فذهبت ثم عادت لا يلزمه شيء ا.هـ. من التنوير وشرحه من الأيمان وفيهما مـن عـوارض الـصـوم. واعلم أن صيغة النذر تحتمل اليمين فلذا كانت ست صور ذكرها بقوله: فإن لم ينو بنذره الصوم شيئاً، أو نــوى الـنـذر فقط أي: من غير تعرض لليمين، أو نوى النذر ونوى أن لا يكون يميناً كان في هذه الصــور نـذراً فقط إجماعاً عملاً بالصيغة وإن نوى اليمين وأن لا يكون نذراً كان يميناً إجماعاً وعليه كفارة يمين إن أفطر وإن نواهما أو نــوى اليمين من غير تعرض للنذر كان نذراً ويميناً، حتى لو أفطر يجب القضاء للنذر والكفارة لليمين عملاً ـ
للثاني، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. ط.

المجاز خلافاً
And if he attaches the vow to a condition, it is not acceptable from him what he did before the existence of his condition. Prayer in Jerusalem, and prayer in the Sacred Mosque is equivalent to a thousand prayers in this mosque of mine. I say: The ruling of the Prophet's mosque is not confined to the spot that was a mosque in his time, because the Prophet said: 'Prayer in this mosque of mine, even if extended to Sana'a, is better than a thousand prayers in other mosques except the Sacred Mosque.' An-Nasa'i related it in Akhbar al-Madina, as in Tartib al-Maqasid al-Hasana of al-Sakhawi. And al-Bazzar narrated with a sound chain that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Prayer in this mosque of mine is better than a thousand prayers elsewhere, except the Sacred Mosque, for it is superior by one hundred thousand prayers.' And in a hadith: 'And the month of Ramadan in this mosque of mine is better than a thousand months elsewhere except the Sacred Mosque.' Al-Bayhaqi narrated it. This is evidence for Ahl al-Sunna that some places have virtue over others, and likewise times. When the Prophet was asked about the best prayer of a woman, he said: 'In the darkest part of her house.' So based on this, it is appropriate that if she undertakes prayer in the Sacred Mosque by vow, and she prays in the darkest part of her house, she would be released from the obligation of her vow, according to what Zufar says, and the evidence is detailed in its place. (And if the vow-maker) attaches (the vow to a condition), like saying: 'If Zayd comes, upon me for Allah is that I give charity a certain amount,' (it is not acceptable from him what he did before the existence of his condition); because what is suspended on a condition does not exist before its existence, and performance is only permissible after the existence of the cause on which the vow was suspended. There remains: if the condition is found, are the time, place, poor person, and dirham specified? The apparent is yes, as in al-Tanwir. Then if he attaches it to a condition he intends, like 'if my absentee comes, I will fulfill when it is found', then he is not fulfilling unless it is in the manner mentioned in his vow. [Supplement] A vow does not fall under a legal ruling; even if he frees a slave in his possession, if he vows to sacrifice his son, he must give a sheep due to the story of al-Khalil (Abraham). If he vows to give charity of ten dirhams worth of bread and gives something else, it is permissible if it equals the ten, like giving its price. He said: 'I vowed' and did not add anything and had no intention, then he must give the expiation of an oath. If he adds the conditional will (mashiyyah), it is invalidated because it invalidates everything attached to the statement, whether worship or transaction. He said: 'If this illness goes away, upon me is such-and-such,' then it goes away and returns, nothing is binding on him. So from al-Tanwir and its commentary on oaths, and in them are from the impediments of fasting. Know that the formula of a vow can also be for an oath, hence there are six scenarios mentioned by his saying: if he does not intend anything with his vow of fasting, or intends only the vow without reference to an oath, or intends the vow and intends that it not be an oath, then in these scenarios it is only a vow by consensus, acting on the formula. If he intends an oath and that it not be a vow, it is an oath by consensus, and he must give the expiation of an oath if he breaks the fast. If he intends both, or intends an oath without reference to a vow, it is a vow and an oath, such that if he breaks the fast, qada' is obligatory for the vow and expiation for the oath, acting on the general application of the metaphor, contrary to... And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 671

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the issue of conditional vows. The starting point is clear: if a person makes a vow conditional on a future event, performing the vowed act before that event occurs does not fulfill the vow. The reason is that the vow is suspended on the condition, and its obligation only arises after the condition is met. The text then digresses into a discussion about the virtue of prayer in the Sacred Mosque and the Prophet's Mosque, citing various hadith. This digression serves to illustrate a related issue: if a woman vows to pray in the Sacred Mosque, according to Zufar, praying in the darkest part of her house (which is the best for a woman) would fulfill her vow because the virtue of that place is greater. However, the main ruling returns: the vow attached to a condition requires the condition to occur for validity. The passage then covers additional details: if the condition is found, the specifics (time, place, recipient) become determined according to the vow. Also, it discusses the intersection of vows and oaths, presenting six scenarios based on the intention of the vower. If the vower has no specific intention, the vow is treated as an oath requiring expiation (kafarah) if violated. If he intends a vow only, it is a vow; if he intends an oath only, it is an oath; if he intends both, both apply. The text ends with a mention of 'amal bil-majaz' (acting on the general application of the metaphor), though the reference is cut off.

Key Terms
تعليق النذر بالشرط (ta'liq al-nadhr bi al-shart): The act of making a vow contingent upon the occurrence of a future event; the vow becomes binding only after the condition is met.
المشيئة (al-mashiyyah): The phrase 'if Allah wills' attached to a vow; according to the passage, it invalidates the vow because it introduces a condition of the divine will, which undermines the commitment.
كفارة يمين (kaffarat yamin): The expiation for breaking an oath: feeding or clothing ten poor people, or freeing a slave, or fasting three days. Here, a vow without specific intention is treated as an oath requiring this expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says: 'When my brother returns from travel, I will give a dirham in charity,' and gives the dirham before the brother returns, what is the ruling?
A) The vow is fulfilled because the charity is given.
B) The vow is not fulfilled; he must give again after the brother returns.
C) The vow is invalid because it was performed before the condition.
D) He must only give the dirham after the brother returns, but the earlier dirham counts as a separate charity.

Key Takeaway
A conditional vow is not fulfilled until the condition occurs; careful attention to one's intention is crucial, as a vague vow may be treated as an oath.

Annulment of Specifications in Vows (Nadhr)
Ruling with proof from Sharh Nur al-Idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifications in vows and apply the principle that specifications are annulled in favor of the essential act of worship.

Core Idea
In a vow (nadhr), the act matters, not the details — time, place, amount, and recipient are annulled.

When a Muslim makes a vow to perform a specific act of worship, they often specify a time, place, or person. But what happens if they fulfill the vow differently? This lesson explains the Hanafi position that the essence of the vow is the act of worship itself, not the attached details. The proof lies in the nature of worship (qurbah) and analogy with obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on fasting a prohibited day in a vow
If someone vows to fast on a day when fasting is prohibited (e.g., Eid), they must break the fast and make it up later. If they fast that day, it is sinful but valid for the vow. This shows the vow's validity despite the prohibition.
The sin is from disregarding the prohibition, not from the vow.
2
State the general principle of annulment
The Hanafi school holds that specifications of time, place, the exact coin (dirham), or the specific poor person are annulled. Any valid performance of the act suffices for the vow.
Specifications are considered for estimation or deferment, not conditions of validity.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
A vow obligates the act itself as an act of worship (qurbah), not the particular details. Worship is defined by its essence (e.g., prayer as humiliation to Allah, fasting as self-restraint), not by location or time.
Obligatory prayers can be performed at home; similarly, a vowed prayer need not be in a specified mosque.
4
Apply the principle to examples
Examples from the text: vowing to fast Sha'ban but fasting Rajab suffices; vowing to pray in Mecca but praying in Egypt suffices; vowing to give a specific dirham but giving another suffices; vowing to give to Zayd but giving to Amr suffices.
The common thread: the act of worship (fasting, prayer, charity) is fulfilled, regardless of specified details.
5
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
Zufr holds that specifications are binding and must be adhered to exactly. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold they are annulled. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view.
The dispute is over the interpretation of the vow's wording and the worshiper's intention.

Source Text

ويجب فِطْرُها وقَضاؤُها وإنْ صامَها أَجْزَاهُ، مَعَ الحُرْمَةِ. وألغينا تعيينَ الزَّمانِ، والمكان، والدرهم، والفقير، فَيُجْزِتَهُ صومُ رَجَبٍ عَنْ نَدْرِهِ صوم شعبان. وتُجْزِئهُ صلاة ركعتين بِمِصْرَ نَذَرَ أداءهما بمكة، والتصدق بدرهم عن درهم عَيَّنَهُ له. والصَّرْفُ لزيد الفقيرِ بنذرِهِ لعَمْرِو.. ارو فعليك بها في فضل النهي، (وَ) لذلك ( يجبُ فِطْرُها) امتثالاً للأمر لئلا يصير بصومهـا مـعـرضـاً عــن ضيافة الكريم، (وَ) يجب (قضاؤُها ) لصحة النذر باعتبار الأصل، (وإن صامها أَجْزَاهُ) الـصـيـام عــن النذر، (مَعَ الحُرْمَةِ الحاصلة من إعراضه عن ضيافة الله تعالى ( وألغينا: تعيين الزَّمانِ و) تعيين ( المكان و ) تعيين (الدرهم و) تعيين (الفقير )؛ لأن النذر إيجاب الفعل في الذمة من حيث هـو قـربـة، لا باعتبار وقوعه في زمان ومكان وفقير، وتعينه للتقدير به أو التأجيل إليه، (فَيُجزئه صوم) شهر رَجَبٍ عَنْ نَدْرِهِ صوم شعبان)؛ لوجود السبب وهو النذر ، والصوم قربة باعتبار اشتماله علـى قـهـر النفس بالإمساك عن شهواتها الله تعالى لا باعتبار وقوعه في شهر بعينه، وتعجيله فيه منفعة له لأنه قد يموت قبل مجيء الوقت، فيحصل ثواب ما قد يفوت، إلا أنه بالإضافة قصد التخفيف على نفسه، حتى إذا مات قبل مجيء ذلك الوقت، لا يلزمه شيء فأعطيناه مقصوده. وتُجزئه صلاة ركعتين) فأكثر إذا صلاهما (بمصْرَ) مثلاً وقد كان (نَذَرَ أداءهما ) أي : أداء صلاتهما بمكة)، أو المسجد النبوي أو بـيـت المقدس؛ لأن صحة النذر باعتبار معنى القربة، وذلك في الصلاة لا في المكان؛ لأن الصلاة تعظيم الله تعالى بجميع البدن، وفي هذا المعنى الأمكنة كلها سواء، وإن كان الأداء في بعض الأمكنة أفضل، فذلك لا يدل على أن الواجب لا يتأدى بدون ذلك، كما في المكتوبات، إذ لا شك إن أداها بالجماعة في المسجد أفضل، وقد أمرنا الشارع بالأداء بهذه الصفة، ومع ذلك إذا أداها منفرداً في بيته سقط عنـه الواجب، والناذر إنما التزم ما هو فعله لا ما ليس فعله، والمكان ليس من فعله فيخرج عن موجب نذره، وإن كان الأداء في المكان الذي عينه أفضل. (وَ) يجزئه ( التصدق بدرهم) لـم يـعـيـن لـه، عــن درهم عينه له) أي: للتصدق المنذور. (و) يجزئه (الصَّرْفُ لزيد الفقـير بـنـذره) أي: مـع نـذره الـصـرف ( لعمرو)؛ لأن معنى العبادة في التصدق باعتبار سد خلة المحتاج، أو إخراج المتصدق ما يجري فيـه الشح عن ملكه، ابتغاء مرضاة الله تعالى، وهذا المعنى حاصل بدون مراعاة تعيين الزمان والمكــان والشخص، خلافاً لزفر رحمه الله تعالى، فإنه يقول بالتعيين. تنبيه: أشرنا إلى فضل البقاع وأفضلها لأداء الصلاة فيها المسجد الحرام، ثم المسجد النبوي، ثم بيت المقدس على ما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ( صَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِ بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ، تَعْدِلُ أَلْفَ صَلاةٍ فيما سواهُ مِنَ المَسَاجِدِ، سَوَى المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ، وَمَسْجِدِي هَذَا، وَصَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا تَعْدِلُ ألف صَلَاةٍ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ، وَصَلَاةٌ فِي المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ تَعْدِلُ أَلْفَ صَلاةٍ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَـذَا ) قلت: وحكــم مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يختص بالبقعة التي كانت مسجداً في زمنه ؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « صَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، وَلَو مَدَّ إِلَى صَنْعَاءَ بِأَلْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيمَا سِوَاهُ مِنَ المَسَاجِدِ إِلا المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ ) قاله النسائي في أخبار المدينة، كذا في « ترتيب المقاصد الحسنة للسخاوي»، وروى البزار بإسناد صحيح أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: صَلَاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيمَا سِوَاهُ، إِلا المَسْجِدَ الحَرَامَ، فَإِنَّهُ يَزِيدُ عَلَيْهِ مَائَةَ أَلْفِ صلاة» (۳) وفي حديث: « وَشَهْرُ رَمَضَانَ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ شَهْرٍ، فِيْمَا سِوَاهُ إِلَّا المَسْجِدِ الحرام ) رواه البيهقي، وهذا دليل لأهل السنة والجماعة، أن لبعض الأمكنة فضيلـة عـلـى بـعـض، وكذا الأزمنة، ولما سئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل صلاة المرأة فقال: « في أشَدَّ مَكانٍ في بيتها ظلمة ، فعلى هذا ينبغي أنها إذا التزمت الصلاة في المسجد الحرام بالنذر، فصلت في أشد مكان في بيتها ظلمة، أن تخرج عن موجب نذرها، على ما يقوله زفر والدليل مبسوط في محله.
And it is obligatory to break it and make it up, and if he fasts it, it suffices him, along with sinfulness. And we annul the specification of time, place, dirham, and poor person, so fasting Rajab suffices for his vow to fast Sha'ban. And praying two rak'ahs in Egypt suffices him if he had vowed to perform them in Mecca, and giving charity with a dirham suffices for a dirham he had specified, and giving to Zayd the poor for his vow to give to Amr... So you must act on the virtue of prohibition. (And) therefore (it is obligatory to break it) in compliance with the command, lest by fasting it he becomes turning away from the hospitality of the Generous. (And) it is obligatory (to make it up) due to the validity of the vow based on the origin. (And if he fasts it, it suffices him) the fasting for the vow, (along with the sinfulness) resulting from his turning away from the hospitality of Allah Almighty. (And we annulled: specification of time, specification of place, specification of dirham, specification of poor person) because the vow is an obligation of the act upon the conscience insofar as it is an act of worship, not due to its occurrence in a time, place, or poor person. Its specification is for estimation or deferment. (So fasting the month of Rajab suffices for his vow to fast Sha'ban) due to the existence of the cause, which is the vow, and fasting is an act of worship insofar as it includes subduing the self by refraining from its desires for Allah Almighty, not due to its occurrence in a specific month. And expediting it is beneficial for him because he may die before the time comes, thus obtaining reward that might be missed. However, in addition, he intends easing for himself, so if he dies before that time comes, nothing is required of him, so we give him his intention. (And praying two rak'ahs suffices him) or more if he prays them (in Egypt) for example, when he had (vowed to perform them) i.e., to pray them (in Mecca), or the Prophet's Mosque or the Sacred House, because the validity of the vow is based on the meaning of closeness, and that is in prayer, not in place. Because prayer is magnifying Allah Almighty with the whole body, and in this meaning all places are equal. Even if performing in some places is better, that does not indicate that the obligation is not fulfilled without that, as in obligatory prayers. There is no doubt that performing them in congregation in the mosque is better, and the Lawgiver commanded performance with this description, yet if he performs them alone in his house, the obligation is dropped from him. The vow-maker only obligated what is his action, not what is not his action, and place is not part of his action, so he exits from the requirement of his vow, even if performing in the place he specified is better. (And) it suffices him (giving charity with a dirham) not specified, (for a dirham he had specified) i.e., for the vowed charity. (And) it suffices him (giving to Zayd the poor with his vow) i.e., with his vow to give (to Amr) because the meaning of worship in charity is either filling the need of the needy or the giver's extraction of what possesses stinginess from his ownership seeking Allah's pleasure. This meaning is achieved without regard to specification of time, place, or person, contrary to Zufr, may Allah have mercy on him, for he insists on specification. Note: We pointed to the virtue of places, the best of them for prayer is the Sacred Mosque, then the Prophet's Mosque, then the Mosque of the Sacred House, as narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A prayer in the Mosque of the Sacred House equals a thousand prayers in other mosques, except the Sacred Mosque and this mosque of mine, and a prayer in this mosque of mine equals a thousand prayers in the Mosque of the Sacred House.' I said: The ruling of the Prophet's Mosque is not confined to the piece of land that was a mosque in his time, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A prayer in this mosque of mine, even if extended to San'a', equals a thousand prayers in other mosques except the Sacred Mosque.' Reported by al-Nasa'i in Akhbar al-Madina, as in Tartib al-Maqasid al-Hasana by al-Sakhawi. And al-Bazzar narrated with a sound chain that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'A prayer in this mosque of mine is better than a thousand prayers elsewhere, except the Sacred Mosque, for it exceeds it by a hundred thousand prayers.' And in a hadith: 'And the month of Ramadan in this mosque of mine is better than a thousand months elsewhere, except the Sacred Mosque.' Reported by al-Bayhaqi. This is evidence for Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a that some places have virtue over others, and likewise times. When the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about the best prayer of a woman, he said: 'In the darkest place of her house.' Accordingly, it is appropriate that if she obligated prayer in the Sacred Mosque by vow, and she prays in the darkest place of her house, that she would exit from the requirement of her vow, according to what Zufr says, and the evidence is extensive in its proper place.
Source pages p. 673

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Nur al-Idah. It addresses the annulment of specifications in vows (nadhr). The key ruling: if someone vows to fast a specific day (like a prohibited day), they must break the fast and make it up; fasting it is sinful but valid. The general principle: specifications of time, place, the exact dirham, or the specific poor person are annulled. The reason is that a vow obligates the act as worship in essence, not tied to particular details. The proof is based on the meaning of worship (qurbah) and analogy with obligatory prayers—place does not affect validity. Examples illustrate: vowing to fast Sha'ban but fasting Rajab suffices; vowing to pray in Mecca but praying in Egypt suffices; vowing to give a specific dirham but another suffices; vowing to give to Amr but giving to Zayd suffices. The commentator notes opposition from Zufr, who insists on specification. A long digression on the virtue of mosques supports the principle that place does not change the essence of the vow. The relied-upon position is the majority Hanafi view that specifications are annulled.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A voluntary vow to perform an act of worship, making it obligatory.
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship drawing one closer to Allah, which is the essence of a vow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on vowing to fast in Rajab but instead fasting in Sha'ban?
A. It is not valid; the specific month must be observed.
B. It is valid and suffices, even though it is better to observe the specified month.
C. It is invalid because Rajab is superior.
D. It requires expiation (kaffarah).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the specification of time, place, amount, or recipient in a vow is not binding; the vow is fulfilled by performing the essential act of worship.

Conditional Vows and the Six Forms of Nadhr
Rulings on conditional vows and classification of nadhr by intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the six forms of nadhr based on intention and apply the ruling on when a conditional vow becomes binding.

Core Idea
A conditional vow is not binding until its condition occurs; intention determines whether it is pure nadhr, yamin, or both.

Vows (nadhr) can be suspended on future conditions, and their legal effect depends critically on the intention of the one making the vow. This lesson unpacks when a conditional vow becomes obligatory, then classifies six distinct scenarios based on the intended combination of nadhr and yamin (oath). Understanding these categories is essential for determining what is required—fulfillment, expiation, or both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional vow
Determine if the vow is suspended on a condition (e.g., 'if Zayd arrives'). Before the condition occurs, the act is not due; after the condition, it becomes wajib.
The condition must be explicitly stated.
2
Determine the specifications after condition
If the vow specifies a time, place, or object, these become binding once the condition is met. The text cites al-Tanwir for this.
Intended details are taken into account.
3
Classify the intention
The formula of nadhr can also imply yamin. Analyze the intention behind the utterance: is it solely nadhr, solely yamin, both, or neither? This yields six forms.
Silence or ambiguous intention defaults to certain categories by consensus.
4
Apply the ruling for the classified form
For pure nadhr (forms 1-3): only fulfillment is required. For pure yamin (form 4): only kaffarah yamin. For combined (forms 5-6): both fulfillment of the nadhr and kaffarah yamin are required upon breaking.
Hanafi position: 'amal bi-umum al-majaz' supports the combined ruling.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and the relied-upon position
The second opinion holds that the formula cannot bear both meanings simultaneously. The Hanafi tarjih adopts the combined ruling as mufta bihi.
The thamarah (practical effect) is the difference in what is owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنْ عَلْقَ النَّدْرَ بشرط لا يُجْزَتُهُ عنه ما فعله قبل وجودِ شَرْطِهِ. بقي ما لو وجد الشرط هل يتعين الزمان والمكان والفقير والدرهم؟ والظاهر نعم لما في التنوير. ثم إن عقله بشرط يريده كإن قدم غائبي يوفي إن وجد ا.هـ فإنه لا يكون موفياً إلا إذا كان على الوجه المذكور في نذره. [ تتمة ] النذر لا يدخل تحت الحكم ولو بعتق رقبة في ملكه نذر أن يذبح ولده فعليه شاة لقصة الخليل علام. نذر أن يتصدق بعشرة دراهم من الخبز فتصدق بغيره جاز إن ساوى العشرة كتصدقه بثمنه، قال علي نذر ولم يزد عليه ولا نية له فعليه كفارة يمين، فإن وصل به المشيئة بطل لأنها تبطل كل ما تعلق بالقول عبادة أو معاملة. قال إن ذهبت هذه العلة فعلي كذا فذهبت ثم عادت لا يلزمه شيء ا.هـ من التنوير وشرحه من الأيمان وفيهما مـن عـوارض الصوم. واعلم أن صيغة النذر تحتمل اليمين فلذا كانت ست صور ذكرها بقوله: فإن لم ينو بنذره الصوم شيئاً، أو نـوى الـنـذر فقط أي: من غير تعرض لليمين، أو نوى النذر ونوى أن لا يكون يميناً كان في هذه الصـور نـذراً فقط إجماعاً عملاً بالصيغة وإن نوى اليمين وأن لا يكون نذراً كان يميناً إجماعاً وعليه كفارة يمين إن أفطر وإن نواهما أو نـوى اليمين من غير تعرض للنذر كان نذراً ويميناً، حتى لو أفطر يجب القضاء للنذر والكفارة لليمين عملاً بعموم المجاز خلافاً للثاني، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. ط.
And if the vow is suspended on a condition, what he did before the existence of its condition does not suffice him. There remains: if the condition occurs, does the time, place, poor person, and dirham become specified? Apparently yes, as in al-Tanwir. Then if he suspends it on a condition he intends, like 'if my absent one arrives, I will fulfill', then if it occurs, he is only fulfilling if it is on the mentioned manner in his vow. [Supplement] The vow does not fall under judgment, even if by freeing a slave in his possession. If he vows to slaughter his son, he must give a sheep due to the story of Khalil, peace be upon him. If he vows to give charity of ten dirhams of bread, and he gives charity with other than it, it is permissible if it equals ten, like giving its price. He said: 'Ali: if he vows and does not increase upon it and has no intention, then upon him is the expiation of an oath. If he attaches the will, it becomes void because it voids everything related to speech, worship or transaction. He said: 'If this illness goes away, upon me is such-and-such,' then it goes away and returns, nothing is required of him. End quote from al-Tanwir and its commentary from al-Ayman, and in both are from the collateral issues of fasting. And know that the formula of nadhr can imply yamin, so there are six forms mentioned by his saying: If he does not intend by his vow anything regarding fasting, or he intends only the nadhr without reference to yamin, or he intends nadhr and intends that it not be yamin—then in these forms it is nadhr only by consensus, acting on the formula. If he intends yamin and that it not be nadhr, it is yamin by consensus, and upon him is the expiation of an oath if he breaks it. If he intends both, or intends yamin without reference to nadhr, it is nadhr and yamin, so if he breaks the fast, qada is required for the nadhr and kaffarah for the yamin, acting on the generality of the metaphor, contrary to the second. And Allah Almighty knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 674

Commentary
This passage covers two main topics: conditional vows and the various forms of nadhr. First, a vow suspended on a condition (e.g., 'If Zayd arrives, I will give charity') is not fulfilled by doing the act before the condition occurs. After the condition, the act becomes obligatory, and if the condition is met, specifications may become binding as per al-Tanwir. Then, a supplement discusses miscellaneous rules: a vow to slaughter a son is invalid and only a sheep is due (following Ibrahim's story); giving charity of bread can be substituted if equal; vows without intention carry kaffarah of an oath; and vows attached to a future event that passes and returns do not require anything. Finally, the six forms of nadhr based on intention are explained: (1) no intention, (2) intention of nadhr only, (3) intention of nadhr and not yamin—these are pure nadhr; (4) intention of yamin only—it is yamin; (5) intention of both—it is both; (6) intention of yamin without reference to nadhr—it is both. The relied-upon position is that combining both incurs both qada (for nadhr) and kaffarah (for yamin).

Key Terms
معلق بالشرط (mu'allaq bi al-shart): A vow suspended on a future condition; not binding until condition occurs.
يمين (yamin): An oath, often with kaffarah for breaking; distinct from nadhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says, 'By Allah, upon me is to fast if Zayd comes,' what is the ruling if they intend both nadhr and yamin?
A. It is only a nadhr.
B. It is only a yamin.
C. It is both, requiring qada and kaffarah.
D. It is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Intention determines whether a vow is a pure nadhr, yamin, or both; a combined vow requires both fulfillment and kaffarah upon breaking.

Conditional Vows: Early Fulfillment Invalid
Ruling on conditional vows with rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fulfilling a conditional vow before its condition and explain the rational proof behind it.

Core Idea
A conditional vow obligates only after the condition; early performance does not fulfill it.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: someone makes a vow dependent on a future event, then performs the act before the event occurs. Is the vow fulfilled? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling based on a rational principle. We will examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is a conditional vow (nadhr mu'allaq). The ruling is that any performance before the condition occurs does not suffice for the vow (ghayr mujzi).
The vow remains pending until the condition is met.
2
Understand the rational proof
The proof is that the obligation is suspended (mu'allaq) on the condition; it does not exist before the condition occurs. Therefore, performing the act before the condition is like performing an act that is not yet required.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, not based on transmitted text.
3
Recognize the practical consequence
If the condition later occurs, the person must perform the vowed act again; the early performance does not discharge the vow. If the condition never occurs, no obligation ever arises.

Source Text

صَلَاةٍ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ، وَصَلَاةٌ فِي المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ تَعْدِلُ أَلْفَ صَلاةٍ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَـذَا ) قلت: وحكــم مسجد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يختص بالبقعة التي كانت مسجداً في زمنه ؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « صَلاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، وَلَو مَدَّ إِلَى صَنْعَاءَ بِأَلْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيمَا سِوَاهُ مِنَ المَسَاجِدِ إِلا المَسْجِدِ الحَرَامِ ) قاله النسائي في أخبار المدينة، كذا في « ترتيب المقاصد الحسنة للسخاوي»، وروى البزار بإسناد صحيح أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: صَلَاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ صَلاةٍ فِيمَا سِوَاهُ، إِلا المَسْجِدَ الحَرَامَ، فَإِنَّهُ يَزِيدُ عَلَيْهِ مَائَةَ أَلْفِ صلاة» (۳) وفي حديث: « وَشَهْرُ رَمَضَانَ فِي مَسْجِدِي هَذَا، أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَلْفِ شَهْرٍ، فِيْمَا سِوَاهُ إِلَّا المَسْجِدِ الحرام ) رواه البيهقي، وهذا دليل لأهل السنة والجماعة، أن لبعض الأمكنة فضيلـة عـلـى بـعـض، وكذا الأزمنة، ولما سئل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن أفضل صلاة المرأة فقال: « في أشَدَّ مَكانٍ في بيتها ظلمة ، فعلى هذا ينبغي أنها إذا التزمت الصلاة في المسجد الحرام بالنذر، فصلت في أشد مكان في بيتها ظلمة، أن تخرج عن موجب نذرها، على ما يقوله زفر والدليل مبسوط في محله. (وإنْ عَلَّق الناذر (النذر بشرط) كقوله: إن قدم زيد فلله عليَّ أن أتصدق بكذا ، ( لا يُجزتُهُ عنه ما فعله قبل وجودِ شَرْطِهِ ) ؛ لأن المعلق بالشرط عـدم قبل وجوده، وإنما يجوز الأداء بعد وجود السبب الذي علق بالنذر به.

And if a vow is suspended on a condition, what he does before the existence of its condition does not suffice for him. ... [long hadith section omitted for brevity] ... Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on conditional vows (nadhr mu'allaq). The author states that if someone makes a vow contingent on a future condition, any performance of the vowed act before the condition occurs does not fulfill the vow. The reasoning is that the obligation is suspended and does not exist until the condition is met. The passage then digresses into the virtues of various mosques as a side note, then returns to additional rulings on vows, including the interaction between vows and oaths. The commentary by the author expands on details such as the necessity of specifying the time, place, and recipient if the condition occurs, and the distinction between a vow and an oath. Finally, it enumerates six scenarios based on the intention of the vow-maker, following the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship or charity, making it obligatory upon oneself.
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the obligation of the vow depends; the vowed act is not required until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
A conditional vow is only fulfilled after its condition occurs; early performance does not discharge the obligation.

Definition and Conditions of I'tikaf
Defines i'tikaf, its conditions, and its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi legal definition of i'tikaf, list its conditions, and distinguish between vowed (wajib) and supererogatory (nafl) i'tikaf.

Core Idea
I'tikaf requires a congregational mosque for men and a home prayer space for women — the place is a condition of validity.

I'tikaf is a spiritual retreat that involves staying in a mosque with intention for worship. The Hanafi school lays down specific conditions regarding the location, intention, and additional requirements for vowed i'tikaf. This lesson unpacks the definition, conditions, and types of i'tikaf as explained in Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Analyse the phrase 'al-iqamah bi-niyyatihi fi masjidi tuqamu fihi al-jama'ah bi al-fi'l li al-salawat al-khams' and note each component: staying, intention, and a mosque with active congregation.
The definition concludes 'so it is not valid in a mosque where congregation is not held'.
2
Distinguish linguistic vs legal meaning
The text gives the linguistic meaning of i'tikaf (staying/adhering) then the legal meaning. Understand how the legal meaning adds specificity: a necessary intention and proper location.
The linguistic root shows both transitive and intransitive uses.
3
List conditions for validity
Extract conditions: Islam, sanity, intention, for men a congregational mosque, for women a designated prayer area at home; for vowed i'tikaf, also fasting and purity from menstruation/post-partum bleeding.
Some conditions apply only to vowed i'tikaf.
4
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The author states 'the pillar is staying (lubth)'. Understand that the rukn is the essence; its omission invalidates i'tikaf entirely.
Conditions (shurut) are external requirements; the rukn is integral.
5
Classify i'tikaf into types
The text mentions three types but focuses on two: wajib (vowed) and nafl (supererogatory). Note the basis: a vow makes it wajib; otherwise it is nafl.
The cause (sabab) for wajib is the vow; for nafl it is the desire for reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۳)

Chapter of I'tikaf. It is: staying with intention in a mosque in which the congregation is actually held for the five prayers. So it is not valid in a mosque where the congregation for prayer is not held, according to the preferred view. And for a woman, i'tikaf is in the mosque of her house, which is the place she designates for prayer. I'tikaf is of three types: obligatory in the vowed...
Source pages p. 675

Commentary
This passage defines i'tikaf (spiritual retreat) linguistically and legally. Linguistically, it means staying and adhering to something. Legally, it is staying with the intention of i'tikaf in a mosque where the five daily prayers are held with congregation. The condition of a congregational mosque is based on hadith from Ali and Hudhayfa. For women, i'tikaf is performed in their designated prayer area at home. The author then outlines the conditions: the pillar (rukn) is staying; the specific mosque and intention are conditions for validity; for a vowed i'tikaf, fasting is a condition. Other conditions include Islam and sanity, but not puberty. Purity from menstruation is required only for vowed i'tikaf. The types are: obligatory (if vowed) and supererogatory (nafl), depending on the motivation. The ruling: if obligatory, it discharges the duty and brings reward; if nafl, only reward.

Key Terms
اعتكاف (i'tikaf): Legally: staying in a mosque with intention, for the purpose of worship, with specific conditions.
مسجد جماعة (masjid jama'ah): A mosque where the five daily prayers are performed with congregation regularly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) In a masjid where the five daily prayers are held with congregation.
C) In a masjid with a minbar.
D) Only in the Prophet's masjid in Madinah.

Key Takeaway
I'tikaf is a worship that requires a specific place: for men, a congregational mosque; for women, a designated prayer area at home; and for vowed i'tikaf, additional conditions of fasting and purity.
